Arbitration by Mutual Consent
Ruling on arbitration with mutual consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on arbitration when both parties agree to the decision.

Core Idea
When both parties agree to an arbitrator's decision, it is valid and binding.

This passage from the chapter of qada' addresses a common scenario: two disputants appoint a third person to arbitrate. The Hanafi school holds that if both parties subsequently agree to the decision, it is legally valid (sahih) and enforceable. This rule underscores the importance of mutual consent in dispute resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
Two parties appoint an arbiter (hakam). He gives a decision. Both parties explicitly agree to that decision.
Agreement must occur after the decision is rendered.
2
State the ruling
The decision is valid (sahih) and binding.
This applies to most civil disputes, not hudud or qisas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو شخصوں نے کسی آدمی کو حکم بنایا اور فیصلہ کر دیا دونوں اس کے فیصلہ سے متفق ہو گئے تو فیصلہ درست ہے
Two persons appointed someone as arbiter and he gave a decision; both agreed to his decision, so the decision is valid.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter of qada (judicial rulings) regarding arbitration (tahkim). When two disputing parties mutually select a third person to arbitrate, and both subsequently consent to the decision he renders, that decision is legally valid and binding. The consent must be explicit after the decision; prior agreement to accept whatever he decides is not sufficient in some views, but here the text emphasizes post-decision agreement.

Key Terms
حکم (hakam): An arbiter appointed by both parties to settle a dispute.
فیصلہ (faisal): The decision or verdict of the arbiter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for the decision of an arbitrator to be valid?
A) That the arbitrator is a qadi appointed by the ruler
B) That both parties agree to his decision after it is given
C) That the dispute is about hudud or qisas
D) That the arbitrator is a relative of both parties

Key Takeaway
Arbitration with mutual consent after decision is valid in Hanafi fiqh.

Revocability of Arbitration and Prohibition in Hudud
Ruling on revoking arbitration and its prohibition in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings on arbitration in Hanafi fiqh: its revocability and its prohibition in hudud and qisas, and identify which cases fall under the prohibition.

Core Idea
Arbitration is revocable always, but forbidden in hudud and qisas.

This lesson clarifies two key principles of arbitration (tahkim) in Hanafi fiqh. First, parties who appoint an arbitrator retain the right to revoke him. Second, this mechanism does not extend to cases involving fixed punishments (hudud) or retaliation (qisas). Understanding these limits ensures arbitration is applied within its proper scope.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling on arbitration
Identify that the default ruling is that arbitration is valid and the appointing parties have the right to revoke the arbitrator at any time, even after he has begun proceedings.
Revocation does not require the arbitrator's consent.
2
Identify the exceptions
Note that arbitration is not permissible in cases of hudud (fixed punishments for crimes like theft, zina) and qisas (retaliation for murder or injury). These must be adjudicated by a qualified qadi.
The prohibition is categorical; even mutual agreement of parties does not make it valid.
3
Apply to scenarios
Given a dispute, determine if it involves property/commercial/family matters (permissible) or hudud/qisas (prohibited). Apply the ruling accordingly.
Examples: theft (hudud) → prohibited; rental contract dispute → permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حکم بنانے والوں کو حکم سے رجوع کا اختیار ہے حدود و قصاص میں تحکیم جائز نہیں
Those who made the arbiter have the option to revoke him; arbitration is not permissible in hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling gives the appointing parties the right to revoke the arbitrator before or even after a decision (if not yet binding). Revocation is valid even if the arbitrator has already begun proceedings. However, arbitration is completely disallowed in cases involving hudud (fixed punishments for crimes like theft, zina) and qisas (retaliation for murder or injury). Such matters must be adjudicated by a properly appointed qadi (judge).

Key Terms
تحکیم (tahkim): The process of appointing an arbitrator to settle a dispute.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Sharia for major sins.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory justice for murder or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which matters is arbitration (tahkim) not permissible according to this text?
A) Commercial disputes
B) Family disputes
C) Hudud and qisas
D) Property disputes

Key Takeaway
Arbitration is revocable at will but absolutely prohibited in hudud and qisas, which require formal judicial proceedings.

The Arbitrator's Duty: Hear Evidence and Administer Oath
Ruling on arbitrator's procedural duties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two procedural duties of an arbitrator under Hanafi law and explain the sequence of evidence and oath when a claim is denied.

Core Idea
Arbitrator must hear evidence and, on denial, decide by oath — mirroring qadi procedure.

This ruling from the Hanafi school establishes the fundamental procedure for arbitration in Islamic law. The arbitrator is not a mere mediator but has adjudicative powers akin to a qadi. When a claim is presented, the claimant must provide evidence; if the defendant denies, the arbitrator cannot simply accept the denial — he must administer an oath and base the judgment on it. This ensures fairness and conformity to Islamic judicial standards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two duties
The passage lists two actions: hearing evidence (bayyinah) and, upon denial, deciding by oath (qasam). Memorize these as the core obligations.
2
Understand the procedural sequence
First the claimant presents evidence. If the defendant denies, the arbitrator administers an oath. The oath is decisive: if the defendant swears, judgment goes in his favor (unless counter-evidence); if he refuses, judgment goes to the plaintiff.
This mirrors the procedure in a Hanafi court (qada).
3
Recognize the legal effect
The oath (qasam) is a legal act that shifts the burden. The arbitrator's decision must be based on this oath, not on personal opinion.
The ruling is wajib on the arbitrator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حکم بینہ کی سماعت کرے اور انکار قسم پر حکم دے دے
The arbiter should hear the evidence and on denial give a decision on oath.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling outlines the procedure for an arbitrator. He is obligated to listen to the evidence (bayyinah) presented by the plaintiff. If the defendant denies the claim, the arbitrator should not simply accept the denial; he should administer an oath to the defendant. The decision should then be based on that oath. This mirrors the procedure in a regular court: the plaintiff provides evidence, and if the defendant denies, the defendant takes an oath, and judgment is given accordingly.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence or proof presented by the claimant.
قسم (qasam): Oath administered to the defendant upon denial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the arbitrator do when the defendant denies the claim?
A) Accept the denial without further action
B) Immediately rule in favor of the plaintiff
C) Administer an oath to the defendant and decide based on it
D) Refer the case to a qadi

Key Takeaway
The arbitrator must follow the same evidentiary procedure as a qadi: hear evidence and, on denial, decide by oath.

Judge's Ruling for Relatives Void
Ruling on a judge ruling for his own close relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a judge adjudicating for his close relatives and identify the legal effect (batil).

Core Idea
A judge's ruling for his own parents, spouse, or children is automatically void.

This lesson establishes a fundamental rule in Islamic judiciary: a qadi cannot judge a case where he has a personal interest through close family ties. The ruling is absolute — any such verdict is legally void (batil) and unenforceable. Understanding this protects the integrity of the judicial process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What is being ruled upon? A judge issuing a judgment in a case.
The act is the judgment itself.
2
Specify the relationships
Which relatives are included? Parents, wife, and children.
The text lists these three categories.
3
State the ruling
What is the legal consequence? The judgment is batil (void).
Void ab initio, no legal effect.
4
Apply the rule
Why is this rule necessary? To prevent bias and maintain judicial integrity.
The case must be referred to another judge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاکم کا اپنے والدین، بیوی، اولاد کے لئے حکم باطل ہے
The ruling of a judge for his parents, wife, and children is void.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling addresses a conflict of interest. A qadi (judge) cannot adjudicate a case where he is related to a party by lineage or marriage. The relationships listed are parents (وَالِدَيْن), wife (بِيوِى), and children (اَولاد). Any judgment he passes in such a case is batil (void) and unenforceable. This is to prevent bias. If such a case arises, it must be referred to another judge.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): Legally void, having no effect.
حاکم (hakim): A judge or ruler with judicial authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of a judge's ruling for his wife?
A) Valid if he is impartial
B) Void (batil)
C) Valid only with consent of the wife
D) Makruh but valid

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling for his immediate family members is void (batil) and must be overturned.

Settlement After Denial is Valid
Ruling on settlement after defendant denies claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on settlement after a defendant denies a claim and identify the key legal principle that permits it.

Core Idea
Even after denial, settlement is valid – a new contract overrides former positions.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in legal disputes: a claimant asserts ownership, the defendant denies, but later the two parties reach a settlement. Is such a settlement valid? The Hanafi school confirms its permissibility, and in this lesson we examine the explicit ruling and its underlying logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their statements
Note the claimant makes a claim, the defendant denies it. This sets the initial conflict.
2
Observe the subsequent action
After denial, the defendant enters into a sulh (settlement) with the claimant. The settlement is a separate contract.
3
State the ruling
The settlement is permissible (ja'iz). The denial does not prevent a valid sulh.
This is the final hukm: mubah and sahih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مدعی نے مکان میں دعوی کیا جس کے قبضہ میں مکان ہے اس نے انکار کر دیا پھر منکر نے مدعی سے اس دعوی میں صلح کر لی تو یہ جائز ہے
A claimant made a claim concerning a house; the person in possession of the house denied it. Then the denier settled with the claimant regarding this claim. So this is permissible.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where someone claims ownership of a house that is in another's possession. The defendant denies the claim. Later, the defendant enters into a sulh (settlement/compromise) with the claimant. Such a settlement is valid (ja'iz). This is permissible because the defendant, by settling, is essentially acknowledging the possibility of the claim and avoiding further dispute. The settlement can involve payment or other terms.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Settlement or compromise between disputing parties.
انکار (inkar): Denial of a claim by the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is a settlement (sulh) valid after the defendant has denied the claim?
A) No, it is invalid
B) Yes, it is permissible
C) Only if the claimant also agrees
D) Only if a judge approves

Key Takeaway
Settlement after denial is valid and permissible as a separate compromise contract.

Confession of Receipt and Claim of Counterfeit
Ruling on burden of proof after iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a confessor's claim of counterfeitness is accepted without proof.

Core Idea
A confession of receipt is binding; a subsequent claim of defect must be proven.

This lesson examines a classic fiqh scenario: a person confesses to receiving a sum of dirhams from another, then later claims those dirhams were counterfeit. The Hanafi school addresses the tension between the binding nature of confession and the need for evidence when asserting a defense. Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal weight of iqrar and the burden of proof in financial claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the claim
Recognize the two statements: first, the confession of receiving dirhams (iqrar of receipt); second, the claim that the dirhams were counterfeit. The confession establishes a prima facie obligation to return the value.
2
Determine the legal effect of the confession
In Hanafi law, a confession (iqrar) is a binding admission against oneself. Once the person admits to receiving the dirhams, he is liable to return the same amount unless he proves a valid defense.
Iqrar is a hujjah against the confessor only.
3
Identify the burden of proof
The claim of counterfeitness is a defense to the obligation. The burden of proof falls on the confessor to prove that the dirhams were counterfeit. Without evidence, his claim is not accepted.
The plaintiff (the original owner) is not required to prove the dirhams were genuine.
4
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that the confessor is not believed without proof. He must bring evidence (baiyinah) or the claim is rejected, and he must repay the genuine value.
Some other schools may consider his claim credible if it is plausible, but the Hanafi position requires proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے اقرار کیا کہ میں نے فلاں شخص سے دس درہم قبضہ کیا پھر اس نے کہا کہ کھوٹے ہیں۔ اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی یا نہیں
A person confessed: I took possession of ten dirhams from a certain person. Then he said: They are counterfeit. Will he be believed or not?
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling presents a question: if someone confesses to receiving a sum of dirhams (silver coins) from another, and then later claims that those dirhams were counterfeit (khotay), will his statement be accepted? The implied answer (based on Hanafi fiqh) is that his word is not necessarily accepted without proof. Since he initially confessed to receipt, that confession establishes a debt. The later claim of counterfeitness is a defense that requires evidence. The burden of proof is on him to prove they were counterfeit. Otherwise, he remains liable to return the genuine value.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission.
کھوٹے (khotay): Counterfeit or defective coins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for the person to succeed in his claim that the dirhams were counterfeit?
A) He must be believed simply because he said so
B) He must prove it with evidence
C) He must return the dirhams first
D) The other person must confirm

Key Takeaway
A confession of receipt creates a binding obligation; a subsequent claim of defect must be proven by the confessor.

The Effect of a Qadi's Dismissal on Previously Issued Orders
Rulings on liability after qadi's dismissal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when an executor of a qadi's order is liable and apply the rules regarding the continued validity of orders after the qadi's dismissal.

Core Idea
A qadi's order executed before dismissal remains valid; the executor is not liable if he acted on a valid order.

This lesson examines the legal consequences when a qadi is dismissed after issuing orders. The key question is whether those orders remain enforceable and whether the executor (ma'mur) can be held liable. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance based on the timing of the order and execution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
Determine what act was ordered (punishment or money transfer) and whether it was carried out. The passage covers both hudud punishments (rajm, cutting, flogging) and financial orders.
2
Determine the timing of the order relative to dismissal
Check whether the qadi's order was given before or after dismissal. Orders given before dismissal remain valid even if execution occurs after dismissal.
3
Evaluate the liability of the executor
If the executor acted on a valid order (given before dismissal), he is not liable (damin). If the qadi later confesses to ordering the act, the executor is still not liable because the order justified the action.
4
Analyze scenarios involving confessions
If both the qadi and the executor confess to the act, the executor becomes liable because the qadi's confession does not override the executor's admission of wrongdoing.
5
Apply the rule for recovery of money
If taken money still exists and the victim confirms the qadi acted during his tenure, the money must be returned to the victim. If the act occurred after dismissal or before appointment, the qadi's statement is still accepted, but liability may shift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی نے کہا کہ میں نے اس پر رجم کا حکم دیا یا اس کا ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم دیا یا کوڑے مارنے کا حکم دیا لہذا یہ کام کر گذر تو شخص مامور کے لئے ان امور کو بجالانے کا حکم قاضی معزول ہو گیا ایک شخص کو کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے ایک ہزار لے کر فلاں کو دئیے تھے اس حال میں کہ اس کے واسطے ایک ہزار درہم کا فیصلہ کیا تھا۔ اس نے کہا کہ یہ در ہم ناحق طور پر لئے تھے تو قاضی کا قول قبول ہو گا ہاتھیہ کاٹنے والے اور مال لینے والے نے اس چیز کا اقرار کیا اور قاضی نے جس کا اقرار کیا وہ بھی ضامن نہ ہوگا مقطوع الید نے اس شخص سے جس سے مال لیا گیا یہ کہا کہ قاضی نے معزول ہونے کے بعد یا قاضی بننے سے پہلے ایسا کیا تو پھر بھی قاضی کا قول معتبر ہو گا قاطع نے اقرار کیا یا مال لینے والے نے اس صورت میں اقرار کیا جس کا قاضی نے اقرار کیا تو دونوں ضامن ہوں گے مال اخذ کے قبضہ میں بعینہ موجود ہو اور اس نے انہی کا اقرار کیا جس کا قاضی نے اقرار کیا اور ماخوذ من المال نے قاضی کی تصدیق کی کہ قاضی نے یہ فعل اپنی قضا کے زمانہ میں کیا یا یہ دعوی کیا کہ غیر قضا کے زمانہ میں کیا تو اس سے مال کیا جائے گا
The qadi said: I ordered rajm on him, or I ordered cutting his hand, or I ordered flogging; so if this act was carried out, then for the person ordered, the order to perform these acts [is valid even if] the qadi is dismissed. To a person he said: I had taken one thousand from you and given to so-and-so while I had decided one thousand dirhams for him. He said: I took these dirhams unjustly. Then the qadi's statement will be accepted. The hand-cutter and the money-taker both confessed to that thing, and what the qadi confessed to, he will not be liable. The one whose hand was cut said to the person from whom money was taken: If the qadi did this after being dismissed or before becoming qadi, then still the qadi's statement is reliable. If the cutter confessed, or the money-taker confessed in this manner that which the qadi confessed, then both will be liable. If the money taken is still in his possession and he confessed exactly what the qadi confessed, and the one from whom money was taken confirmed that the qadi did this during his tenure of judgeship, or claimed that he did it outside of judgeship, then the money will be taken from him.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of a qadi's dismissal on his previously issued orders and the liability of those who execute them. The passage presents several rulings: First, if a qadi orders a punishment (rajm, hand-cutting, flogging) and the order is carried out, then even if the qadi is later dismissed, the executor is not liable because he acted on a valid order. Second, if a qadi states that he took money from someone and gave it to another as part of a judgment, his statement is accepted if he claims it was a rightful decision. Third, if the executor (hand-cutter or money-taker) confesses to the act, but the qadi also confesses to ordering it, the executor is not liable because the order justified his action. Fourth, if the victim (the one whose hand was cut or money taken) claims the qadi acted after dismissal or before appointment, the qadi's statement is still accepted as authoritative. Fifth, if both the qadi and the executor confess, the executor becomes liable because the qadi's confession does not absolve him. Finally, if the taken money is still in existence and the taker confesses, and the victim confirms the qadi acted during his tenure, the money is taken from the taker and returned. These rulings emphasize the authority of the qadi's orders within his jurisdiction and the conditions under which executors are protected or held liable.

Key Terms
قاضی (qadi): A judge appointed to adjudicate disputes and enforce Islamic law
مامور (ma'mur): The person ordered by the qadi to execute a punishment or action
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation or responsibility

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a qadi orders hand-cutting and the executor does it, but later the qadi confesses that he had no right to order it, what is the ruling?
A) The executor is liable because the order was invalid.
B) The executor is not liable because the order was given and executed.
C) The executor is liable only if the victim complains.
D) The qadi must compensate the victim directly.

Key Takeaway
An executor who follows a qadi's valid order is not liable even if the qadi is later dismissed or confesses to error, except when both confess.

8 min
The Definition of Qada in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition of qada and introduction to adab al-qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qada in Hanafi fiqh, distinguishing its linguistic and technical meanings, and identify the key condition of wilayat 'ammah.

Core Idea
Qada is a binding statement from one with general authority — without wilayat 'ammah, there is no valid judgment.

This passage opens the Book of Adab al-Qadi, explaining why qada follows transactions: to resolve disputes. Before diving into the judge's conduct, the author defines qada precisely. Understanding this definition is foundational to all later rules of judgeship. Let's unpack the Hanafi technical meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
The text states that qada literally means 'to make binding'. This is the root.
2
Extract the technical definition
In Shari'ah, qada is a binding statement (qawl mulzim) issued from general authority (wilayat 'ammah). Note the two components: the statement itself and the authority behind it.
3
Understand the role of wilayat 'ammah
Only a person with general authority (over all people and all matters) can issue a valid qada. This excludes muftis and arbitrators.
Wilayat 'ammah is a necessary condition.
4
Connect adab to the definition
Adab al-qadi means the judge must adhere to praiseworthy Shari'ah traits, which flows from the seriousness of the binding statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب ادب القاضي
ترجمہ یہ کتاب ادب القاضی کے بیان میں ہے
كتاب الادب القاضي
تشریح چونکہ بیوع و کفالات وغیرہ معاملات میں اکثر جھگڑے پیدا ہوتے ہیں اس لئے ان کے بعد ایسی چیز کو بیان فرمایا جو منازعات کو قطع کرنے والی ہے۔ اور وہ قضا ہے۔ ادب کے معنی اخلاق جمیلہ اور خصال حمیدہ سے آراستہ ہونا۔ اور قضا کے لغوی معنی لازم کرنا اور شریعت میں قضا وہ قول ملزم ہے جو ولایت عامہ سے صادر ہو یعنی جس شخص کو ولایت عامہ حاصل ہے اس سے صادر ہو کر جو اس قول کا مخاطب ہے اس پر لازم ہو۔ ادب القاضی سے ایسے امور مراد ہیں جو شرعاً محمود ہوں قاضی اُن کو لازم پکڑے۔ مثلاً انصاف کو عام کرنا ظلم کو ختم کرنا، حدود شرع اور سنت پر قائم رہنا۔ قضا کتاب اللہ بسنت رسول، اجماع اور عقل چاروں دلیلوں سے مشروع اور ثابت ہے۔ کتاب اللہ جیسے اللہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے: (وان احكم بينهم بما انزل الله) - (فاحكم بين الناس بالحق ولا تتبع الهوى) (انا انزلنا التوراة فيها هدى و نور يحكم بها النبيون)
سنت رسول کا یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی اور حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ عنہما کو قاضی بنا کر بھیجا گیا تھا۔ اور حضرت معاذ سے رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا تھا: (هم تقضی یا معاذ؟ فقال بكتاب الله قال فإن لم تجد قال بسنة رسول الله) قال فان لم تجد قال أجتهد براني قال الحمد لله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله لما يرضى رسول الله)
قضا کی مشروعیت پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع بھی ثابت ہے اور عقل کے ذریعہ اس طرح ثابت ہے کہ قضاء بالحق میں عدل ظاہر ہوگا۔ ظالم کا ظلم دور ہوگا اور مظلوم کو انصاف ملے گا۔ اور سیاسی چیزیں ہیں جن کی طرف ہر عاقل کی عقل دعوت دیتی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ عقلاً بھی قضاء ثابت ہے۔
Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Translation: This book is about the etiquette of the judge. Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Explanation: Since disputes often arise in sales, guarantees, and other transactions, after them a thing is mentioned that cuts off disputes, and that is qada. The meaning of adab is to be adorned with beautiful morals and praiseworthy qualities. The literal meaning of qada is to make binding, and in Shari'ah, qada is a binding statement issued from general authority, i.e., it issues from a person who has general authority, and it becomes binding on the addressee. By 'adab al-qadi' is meant matters that are praiseworthy in Shari'ah, which the judge must hold onto. For example, spreading justice, ending oppression, adhering to Shari'ah limits and the Sunnah. Qada is established and proven by four proofs: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, Ijma, and reason. From the Book of Allah, like Allah Almighty said: (And judge between them by what Allah has revealed) - (So judge between the people by truth and do not follow desire) (Indeed, We sent down the Torah, in which was guidance and light, by which the prophets judged.) From the Sunnah of the Messenger: Ali and Mu'adh were sent as judges, and the Prophet said to Mu'adh: 'How will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will exert my opinion (ijtihad).' He said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases the Messenger of Allah.' The consensus of the Muslims is also established on the legitimacy of qada, and through reason it is established in that judging with truth manifests justice, removes the oppression of the oppressor, and gives justice to the oppressed. And these are political matters that every rational mind calls towards. So it is understood that qada is also proven by reason.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage serves as the opening of the Book of the Etiquette of the Judge (Kitab Adab al-Qadi). The commentator explains why this book follows the Book of Sales and Guarantees: because disputes arise in transactions, and qada (judging) is what resolves them. He defines 'adab' as good character and praiseworthy traits, and 'qada' linguistically as making something binding. In Shari'ah, qada is a binding statement issued by one who has general authority (wilayat 'ammah). The purpose of adab al-qadi is to list praiseworthy actions that a judge must adhere to, such as spreading justice, ending oppression, and adhering to Shari'ah limits and Sunnah. The commentator then establishes the legitimacy (mashru'iyyah) of qada through four proofs: the Quran (citing three verses), the Sunnah (citing the hadith of Mu'adh when he was sent to Yemen), Ijma' (consensus of the Muslims), and reason (aql) which shows that judging with justice is inherently good and oppression is evil, which every rational person recognizes. The passage ends by affirming that qada is established by all four sources.

Key Terms
قضا (qada): A binding statement (qawl mulzim) issued by one who has general authority (wilayat 'ammah) in Shari'ah.
ادب القاضي (adab al-qadi): The praiseworthy traits and actions that a judge must adhere to in Shari'ah.
ولایت عامہ (wilayat 'ammah): General authority to govern and judge over all people in all matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is a necessary condition for a statement to be considered qada in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is based on Quran and Sunnah.
B) It is issued by a person with general authority.
C) It is in writing.
D) It is accepted by both parties.

Key Takeaway
Qada is defined as a binding statement issued by one with general authority — without wilayat 'ammah, there is no qada.

The Four Proofs for the Legitimacy of Qada
Proofs for the legitimacy of qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, reason) cited by the Hanafi school for the legitimacy of qada and explain how each proof establishes its mashru'iyyah.

Core Idea
Qada is legitimized by Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and reason — a ruling with fourfold evidentiary support.

Having defined qada, the text now establishes its legitimacy through the four primary sources of Shari'ah. This is a classic Hanafi demonstration of mashru'iyyah using the full spectrum of legal proofs. The Quran provides direct commands, the Sunnah shows prophetic practice, Ijma confirms consensus, and reason (aql) affirms intrinsic justice.

Guided Path
1
List the four proofs
The text states Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and reason ('aql). Identify each.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Three verses are cited: Judge by what Allah revealed, judge with truth, and the Torah verse. Note that these command judgment.
The verses establish the obligation of judging by divine law.
3
Examine the Sunnah evidence
The hadith of Mu'adh when sent to Yemen shows the Prophet (s) appointed a judge and approved his method.
This indicates the permissibility and legitimacy of qada.
4
Understand Ijma and reason
Ijma: Muslims have always appointed judges. Reason: Justice is inherently good and oppression inherently evil, as recognized by rational minds.
Ijma provides collective authority; reason provides rational basis.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul
The Hanafi school ranks proofs: Quran and Sunnah are primary, Ijma is a source, and reason is used as a supplemental proof (istihsan or maqasid).
This shows the comprehensive approach of Hanafi methodology.

Source Text

The Fasiq Judge: Validity of Appointment and Judgments
Inter-madhhab dispute on fasiq judge's qualification and judgment validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the fasiq judge's eligibility and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A fasiq's judgeship is valid in Hanafi law but he deserves removal.

The appointment of a qadi carries heavy responsibility. This passage confronts a sensitive question: what if the judge himself is a fasiq – a sinner? The Hanafi school navigates between upholding the finality of judgments and maintaining judicial integrity. You will explore how the ruling is derived by analogy to testimony and why the Shafi'i school dissents.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: a fasiq is eligible for qada; if appointed, his judgments are valid (sahih), but it is not recommended. If a just judge becomes fasiq, he is not automatically removed but deserves removal.
The text uses 'لا ينعزل ويستحق العزل' – not removed but deserves removal.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State Imam al-Shafi'i's position: a fasiq's qada is invalid, just as his testimony is rejected. This is based on analogy to shahada.
Shafi'i school rejects fasiq's testimony entirely, so by qiyas, his judgeship is also void.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since a fasiq's testimony is invalid, his authority as judge – which is even greater – must also be invalid. The analogy (qiyas) from shahada is direct.
The Shafi'i view treats the condition of 'adalah as essential for both shahada and qada.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis distinguish between the initial appointment and the validity of judgments. Even though a fasiq should not be appointed, his judgments once rendered are effective to maintain legal stability. The analogy to shahada is accepted, but Hanafis hold that a fasiq's testimony, if accepted by the judge, is technically valid.
Hanafis emphasize the practical consequence: overturning all judgments of a fasiq judge would cause chaos.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, judgments of a fasiq judge are enforceable and cannot be overturned on grounds of his fasiq status. In the Shafi'i school, such judgments would be null and void, requiring retrial.
This affects the stability of legal decisions and the security of litigants' rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عہدہ قضا کیلئے شرائط، فاسق قاضی بن سکتا ہے یا نہیں اگر قاضی بن کر فسق کا ارتکاب کرے تو قابل معزول ہے یا نہیں
قال ولا تصح ولاية القاضى حتى يجتمع فى المولى شرائط الشهادة ويكون من اهل الاجتهاد اما الاول فلان حكم القضا يستقى من حكم الشهادة لان كل واحد منهما من باب الولاية فكل من كان اهلا للشهادة يكون اهلاً للقضاء وما يشترط الاهلية الشهادة يشترط لاهلية القضاء والفاسق اهل للقضاء حتى لو قلد يصح الا انه لا ينبغى ان يقلد كما في حكم الشهادة فانه لا ينبغى ان يقبل القاضى شهادته ولو قبل جاز عندنا ولو كان القاضي عدلا ففسق باخذ الرشوة او غيره لا ينعزل ويستحق العزل وهذا هو ظاهر المذهب وعليه مشائخنا رحمهم الله وقال الشافعى الفاسق لا يجوز قضاؤه كما لا يقبل شهادته عنده وعن علمائنا الثلاثة الله في النوادر انه لا يجوز قضاؤه وقال بعض المشائخ اذا قلد الفاسق ابتداء يصح ولو قلد
Conditions for the office of qada: Can a fasiq become a judge? If he becomes a judge and commits fasiq, is he liable to removal? He said: The authority of the judge is not valid until the person possesses the conditions of testimony and is a mujtahid. As for the first (verdicts), because the ruling of qada is derived from the ruling of testimony, since each is from the category of authority. So whoever is eligible for testimony is eligible for qada, and what is required for eligibility for testimony is required for eligibility for qada. And the fasiq is eligible for qada, so if he is appointed it is valid, but he should not be appointed, just as in the case of testimony: the judge should not accept his testimony, but if he accepts, it is permissible according to us. And if the judge was just and then becomes fasiq by taking a bribe or otherwise, he is not removed but deserves removal. This is the apparent school (zahir al-madhhab), and upon it are our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them). Al-Shafi'i said: The fasiq's qada is not permissible, just as his testimony is not accepted according to him. And from our three scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) is a narration in al-Nawadir that his qada is not permissible. And some scholars said: If a fasiq is initially appointed, it is valid, and if he is appointed (after becoming fasiq) it is also valid.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the appointment of a judge and specifically addresses the ruling regarding a fasiq (sinner) judge. It begins by stating that the authority (wilayah) of a judge is not valid unless the person possesses the conditions of a witness (shara'it al-shahada) and is a mujtahid. The reason given is that the ruling of qada is derived from the ruling of shahada (testimony) because both are types of authority (wilayah). Therefore, whoever is qualified for shahada is qualified for qada, and what is required for eligibility in shahada is required for eligibility in qada. The text then declares that a fasiq is eligible (ahl) for qada in the sense that if he is appointed, his appointment is valid (sahih), but it is not befitting to appoint him. This is similar to shahada, where a judge should not accept the testimony of a fasiq, but if he does accept it, it is permissible (ja'iz) in our school. If a judge who was just (adl) becomes fasiq by taking bribes or otherwise, he is not automatically removed from office, but he deserves to be removed. This is the zahir al-madhhab (apparent position of the school) and the view of our scholars. Then the text contrasts the view of Imam Shafi'i, who holds that a fasiq's qada is not valid just as his testimony is not accepted. It also mentions a narration (riwayah) from our three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in al-Nawadir that a fasiq's qada is not valid. Some scholars said that if a fasiq is initially appointed, it is valid, but if he is appointed after the fact, it is also valid.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists on minor sins, lacking 'adalah (moral integrity). In this passage, it refers to a person who is not just or upright.
شرائط الشهادة (shara'it al-shahada): The conditions required for a witness to be eligible: being Muslim, adult, sane, free, and just ('adl). The text analogizes these to qualifications for a judge.
اهل الاجتهاد (ahl al-ijtihad): A person capable of deducing legal rulings from primary sources independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab as stated in this passage, what is the ruling if a just judge becomes fasiq by taking a bribe?
A) His judgments become void immediately
B) He is automatically removed from office
C) He is not removed but deserves removal
D) He must repent but can continue without penalty

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a fasiq judge's judgments are valid and enforceable, though the judge himself deserves removal and should not have been appointed.

Qada — Judiciary

The Conditions for a Qadi and the Validity of a Fasiq Judge
Conditions for qadi and ruling on fasiq judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions required for a qadi according to the Hanafi school, and explain why a fasiq's appointment as judge is valid yet blameworthy, evaluating the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A fasiq's judgeship is valid but blameworthy: 'adala is a condition of perfection, not of validity, in both testimony and judgment.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we explore the foundational conditions for a judge in Islamic law and a distinctive Hanafi position: that a fasiq (sinner) can be a valid judge, though it is not recommended. We will trace the author's reasoning, which draws an analogy between testimony (shahada) and judgment (qada), and then confront the Shafi'i objection. By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi school treats 'adala as a condition of perfection (kamaal) rather than validity (sihha) — a principle with far-reaching legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for a qadi from the matn
The matn of al-Quduri states that a judge must possess the qualifications of a witness and be a mujtahid. List the specific conditions mentioned in the commentary: Islam, adulthood, sanity, freedom, not blind, not convicted of qadhf, and ideally just, chaste, and knowledgeable. Note that 'adala is recommended, not required for validity.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas) between shahada and qada
The author argues that qada is derived from shahada because both involve wilaya (authority to bind others). Since a fasiq's testimony is accepted in Hanafi law, his judgeship is also valid. Trace the logical chain: shahada conditions → qada conditions; fasiq qualifies for testimony → fasiq qualifies for qada.
This qiyas is based on the common illa of wilaya.
3
Locate the Hanafi position on the fasiq judge and its proof
The zahir al-madhhab states: a fasiq is qualified for qada; if appointed, it is valid but blameworthy. If a just judge becomes fasiq, he is not automatically dismissed but deserves dismissal. The proof is qiyas on shahada, supported by the hadith of Mu'adh and the absence of explicit prohibition.
The text cites the hadith of Mu'adh to establish the legitimacy of ijtihad, not directly fasiq.
4
Compare with Shafi'i and intra-Hanafi differences
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a fasiq's qada is invalid, just as his testimony is invalid. Additionally, a Nawadir narration from the three Hanafi imams also invalidates it. Some mashayikh distinguish based on the timing of fisq: if appointed while just, he is dismissed upon becoming fasiq.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf shows the range of scholarly opinion within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the zahir al-madhhab: a fasiq's appointment is valid and he is not automatically dismissed. The practical consequence: judgments issued by a fasiq judge are enforceable and cannot be overturned solely due to his fisq. However, the appointing authority should remove him.
This prevents legal chaos while upholding the ideal of judicial integrity.

تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی آدمی کو قاضی بنانا اُسی وقت جائز ہوگا جب کہ اس میں شہادت کی تمام شرطیں موجود ہوں ۔ مثلاً مسلمان ہو ، بالغ ہو ، عاقل ہو ، آزاد ہو اور نا بینا اور محدود فی القذف نہ ہو۔ اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ عادل ہو، عفیف ہو ، عالم بالسنہ ہو اور اپنے سے پہلے قاضیوں کے طریق پر ہو۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ جس کو عہدہ قضاء سپرد کیا جا رہا ہے وہ اہل اجتہاد میں سے ہو ۔ حاصل یہ کہ قاضی کے واسطے شہادت اور اجتہاد کا اہل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ قاضی کے اندر شہادت کی شرطوں کا پایا جانا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ حکم قضاء حکم شہادت سے مستفاد ہے۔ کیونکہ قضاء اور شہادت دونوں باب ولایت سے ہیں ۔ اور ولایت کہتے ہیں تحفیظ القول علی الغیر ۔ پس جس طرح شاہد اپنا قول غیر پر نافذ کرتا ہے اسی طرح قاضی بھی اپنا قول غیر پر نافذ کرتا ہے۔اور ولایت قضا ولایت شہادت سے چونکہ عام اور اکمل ہے۔ اس لئے ولایت قضا کے واسطے شرائط شہادت کا ہونا بدرجہ اولی ضروری ہے اور جو شخص شہادت کا اہل ہوگا وہ قاضی بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور اہلیت شہادت کے واسطے جو چیزیں شرط ہیں اہلیت قضا کے لئے بھی شرط ہوں گی ۔ پس فاسق چونکہ شہادت کا اہل ہے اسلئے وہ قاضی بننے کا بھی اہل ہوگا۔ حتی کہ فاسق کو قاضی بنا دیا گیا تو جائز ہے لیکن اس کو قاضی بنا نا مناسب نہیں ہے جیسا کہ قاضی کے لئے فاسق کی گواہی قبول کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر فاسق کی گواہی قبول کر لی گئی تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ عدالت شرائط شہادت میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ شہادت کے مناسبات میں سے ہے۔ اور اگر قاضی عادل ہو لیکن رشوت لینے یا ، شراب پینے یا زنا وغیرہ کی وجہ سے فاسق ہو گیا تو معزول نہ ہو گا۔ البتہ معزولی کا مستحق ہو جائے گا ۔ اور جب تک معزول نہیں کیا جائے
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9 [PAGE_244] Kitab Adab al-Qadi. Translation: This book is about the etiquette of the judge. Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi. Commentary: Since frequent disputes arise in transactions, sales, guarantees etc., after them a thing that cuts off disputes is mentioned, and that is qada. Adab means to be adorned with beautiful morals and praiseworthy qualities. Qada linguistically means to make binding, and in Shari'ah it is a binding statement issued by one with general authority, i.e., issued by the one who has general authority and binding upon the one addressed. By Adab al-Qadi is meant matters that are praiseworthy in Shari'ah which the judge must adhere to, e.g., spreading justice, ending oppression, adhering to Shari'ah limits and Sunnah. Qada is legislated and established by four proofs: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, Ijma', and reason. From the Book of Allah, Allah Almighty said: 'And judge between them by what Allah has revealed' (5:49), 'So judge between the people with truth and do not follow desire' (38:26), 'Indeed We sent down the Torah, in which was guidance and light; the prophets judged by it' (5:44). From the Sunnah of the Messenger: Ali and Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with them) were sent as judges. The Prophet said to Mu'adh: 'How will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find [it there]?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find [it there]?' He said: 'I will exert my opinion (ijtihad).' The Prophet said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases the Messenger of Allah.' There is also Ijma' of the Muslims on the legislation of qada, and by reason it is established because in qada bil haqq justice appears, the oppression of the oppressor is removed, the oppressed gets justice, and these are political things to which every rational person's intellect invites. So it is known that qada is established by reason. Conditions for the office of qada: Can a fasiq become a judge? If a judge commits fisq, is he liable to dismissal? He (al-Quduri) said: 'The appointment of a judge is not valid until the conditions of testimony are met in the appointee and he is among the people of ijtihad. As for the first, because the ruling of qada is derived from the ruling of testimony, since each of them is of the category of wilayah (authority). So whoever is qualified for testimony is qualified for qada, and what is required for qualification of testimony is also required for qualification of qada. The fasiq is qualified for qada, so if he is appointed it is valid, but he should not be appointed, just as in the ruling of testimony: the judge should not accept his testimony, but if he accepts it, it is permissible according to us. If the judge was just but then became fasiq by taking a bribe or otherwise, he is not dismissed but deserves dismissal. This is the apparent madhhab, and our mashayikh (may Allah have mercy on them) are upon it. Al-Shafi'i said: The fasiq's qada is not permissible, just as his testimony is not accepted according to him. From our three imams [Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Hasan ibn Ziyad?] there is a narration in al-Nawadir that his qada is not permissible. Some mashayikh said: If a fasiq is appointed initially, it is valid; but if he was appointed while just and then becomes fasiq, he is dismissed because the one who appointed him relied on his justice and was not content with his appointment without it. And can a fasiq be a mufti? It was said: No, because it is a religious matter and his report is not accepted in religious matters. And it was said: He is suitable, because the fasiq will exert himself cautiously to avoid being attributed to error.' Translation of the commentary: Sahib Quduri says that appointing someone as judge is only valid when all conditions of testimony are present in him, e.g., Muslim, adult, sane, free, not blind, not convicted of qadhf. And it is better that he be just, chaste, knowledgeable in the Sunnah, and follow the way of previous judges. The second thing is that the one being entrusted with the office of qada must be among the people of ijtihad. The conclusion is that it is necessary for the judge to be qualified for testimony and ijtihad. The presence of the conditions of testimony in the judge is necessary because the ruling of qada is derived from the ruling of testimony, because qada and testimony both fall under the category of wilayah. Wilayah means enforcement of a statement upon another. Just as a witness enforces his statement upon another, so does a judge enforce his statement upon another. And since the wilayah of qada is more general and complete than the wilayah of testimony, the presence of the conditions of testimony for the wilayah of qada is a fortiori necessary. Whoever is qualified for testimony can also be a judge. What is required for qualification of testimony is also required for qualification of qada. So since the fasiq is qualified for testimony, he is also qualified to be a judge. Even if a fasiq is appointed judge, it is valid, but it is not appropriate to appoint him, just as it is not appropriate for a judge to accept the testimony of a fasiq. However, if the testimony of a fasiq is accepted, it is permissible according to us because 'adala is not among the conditions of testimony but among its appropriateness. If a judge is just but becomes fasiq due to bribery, drinking wine, adultery, etc., he is not dismissed but becomes deserving of dismissal. And as long as he is not dismissed, his rulings are valid.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the matn of al-Quduri regarding the Kitab Adab al-Qadi. The author first establishes the legitimacy of qada (judgeship) through the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and reason. He then presents the matn stating the conditions for a valid qadi: the appointee must possess the same qualifications required for a witness (shahada) and must be a mujtahid. The reasoning is that qada and shahada both involve wilaya (authority to bind others), so whoever can be a witness can be a judge. The passage then addresses the specific issue of a fasiq (sinner) judge. The Hanafi position (zahir al-madhhab) is that a fasiq is AhL (qualified) for qada; if appointed, the appointment is valid, though it is not appropriate (la yanbaghi). Similarly, if a just judge becomes fasiq, he is not automatically removed (la yan'azil) but deserves dismissal (yastaḥiqqu al-'azl). The text contrasts this with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that a fasiq's qada is invalid. It also mentions a narration in Nawadir from the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad? Actually 'our three imams' likely refers to the three main Hanafi imams but the Nawadir narration is from them that fasiq's qada is invalid, though this is a weaker position). Some mashayikh differentiate based on the circumstances of appointment: if initially appointed as fasiq, valid; if appointed as just and then becomes fasiq, he is dismissed because the appointer relied on his justice. Finally, the passage discusses whether a fasiq can be a mufti, with two opinions: one that he cannot because religious matters require trustworthy reports, and another that he can because he will be extra cautious to avoid error. The commentary reinforces that 'adala (justice) is a condition of appropriateness (kamaal) not of validity (sihha) in both shahada and qada, which is a distinctive Hanafi principle.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): A binding statement (qawl mulzim) issued by one with general authority (wilaya 'amma), which is binding upon the person to whom it is addressed.
ولاية (wilaya): Authority to enforce one's statement upon another (tahfiz al-qawl 'ala al-ghayr). Both shahada and qada are types of wilaya.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins (kaba'ir) or persists in minor sins, lacking 'adala (justice). In this context, a person whose testimony is not recommended but still valid.
عدالة ('adala): Justice or uprightness; a moral quality that makes one's testimony reliable. In this passage, it is considered a condition of appropriateness (kamaal) not of validity (sihha) for shahada and qada.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court; a statement of knowledge that creates legal obligation. The qualifications for a witness are analogous to those for a judge.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Exerting one's utmost effort in deriving legal rulings from the primary sources. A qadi must be a mujtahid (capable of ijtihad) to rule independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab as presented in this text, if a judge who was just ('adil) becomes fasiq by taking a bribe, what happens to his position?
A) He is immediately and automatically dismissed, and all his previous judgments are invalid.
B) He is not automatically dismissed but deserves removal; his rulings remain valid until he is actually dismissed.
C) He is dismissed only if the caliph or appointing authority issues a specific decree of removal.
D) He cannot be dismissed because the appointment was initial and unconditional.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a fasiq can be a valid judge because 'adala is a condition of perfection, not validity; a judge who becomes fasiq is not automatically dismissed, ensuring legal stability.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
The Validity of a Fasiq as Qadi: Hanafi Position and Dispute
Commentary on qualifications of a qadi and effect of fisq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on appointing a fasiq as qadi, explain the qiyas with testimony, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i argument.

Core Idea
A fasiq can be a qadi: his appointment is valid but not preferred, just like his testimony.

This lesson examines the qualifications of a judge, specifically whether a sinful person (fasiq) can hold judicial office. The Hanafi school, uniquely, permits it but strongly discourages it. We'll explore the reasoning and the cross-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on a fasiq qadi
Identify that the Hanafi school holds appointing a fasiq as qadi to be valid (sahih) but not preferable. If a just qadi becomes fasiq, he is not automatically removed unless stipulated.
2
Identify the dalil (qiyas with testimony)
The Hanafi proof is analogy (qiyas) with testimony: since a fasiq's testimony is valid (justice is not a condition), his judgment is also valid because both share the basis of wilayah (authority).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some mashayikh hold automatic removal if a just qadi becomes fasiq; a nawadir narration from the three imams says fasiq's judgment is invalid. The relied-upon position (zahir al-madhhab) is the validity of appointment and no automatic removal.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali view
The opposing schools hold that a fasiq cannot be a qadi by analogy with their view that a fasiq's testimony is invalid. The Hanafi response: justice is not a condition for testimony in our school; it is only a preference.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The mufta bihi is that a fasiq's appointment is valid, and his rulings are effective until removal. The thamarah al-khilaf: in Shafi'i practice, a fasiq qadi is invalid; in Hanafi, he is valid though discouraged.

کتاب الادب القاضي
وهو عدل ينعزل بالفسق لان المقلد اعتمد عدالته فلم يكن راضياً بتقليده دونها وهل يصلح الفاسق مفتياً قيل لا لانه من امور الدين وخبره غير مقبول في الديانات وقيل يصلح لانه يجتهد الفاسق حذراً عن النسبة الى الخطأ
ترجمہ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ قاضی کومتوئی کرنا ہی نہیں ہوتا یہاں تک کہ جس کو متولی کیا اس میں گواہی کی شرطیں موجود ہوں اور وہ اہل اجتہاد میں سے بھی ہو ۔ بہر حال اول تو اس لئے کہ حکم قضاء بھی حکم شہادت سے سیراب کیا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک ولایت کے قبیل سے ہے۔ پس جو شخص شہادت کا اہل ہوگا وہ قضا کا بھی اہل ہوگا۔ اور جو چیز اہلیت شہادت کے واسطے شرط ہے وہ الملیت قضاء کے لئے بھی شرط ہے۔ اور فاسق ، قضاء کا اہل ہے حتی کہ اگر اس کو قاضی بنایا گیا تو صحیح ہے مگر فاسق کو قاضی بنانا مناسب نہیں ہے جیسے شہادت کے حکم میں ہے۔ کیونکہ قاضی کو فاسق کی گواہی قبول کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر فائق کی گواہی قبول کر لی تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اور اگر قاضی عادل ہو لیکن رشوت لینے کی وجہ سے یا اس کے علاوہ کسی وجہ سے فاسق ہو گیا تو وہ معزول نہ ہوگا اور عزل کا مستحق ہوگا۔ اور یہی ظاہر مذہب ہے اور اس پر ہمارے مشائخ مھم اللہ ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس کی شہادت قبول نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ اور ہمارے علمائے ثلاثہ سے نوادر کی روایت ہے کہ فاسق کی قضا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ جب فاسق کو ابتداء قاضی بنا دیا گیا تو صحیح ہے۔ اور اگر عادل ہونے کی حالت میں قاضی بنایا گیا تو فسق کی وجہ سے معزول ہو جائے گا ۔ اس لئے مقلد ( قاضی بنانے والے) نے اس کے عادل ہونے پر اعتماد کیا تھا۔ پس بغیر عدالت کے اس کو قاضی بنانے پر راضی نہیں ہو گا ۔ "اچھا فاسق آدمی مفتی ہو سکتا ہے۔ کہا گیا کہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ فتوی دینی امور میں سے ہے اور دینی امور میں فاسق کی خبر غیر مقبول ہے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ فاسق کا مفتی ہونا صحیح ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ غلطی کی طرف منسوب ہونے کے ڈر سے فاسق کوشش کرے گا۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی آدمی کو قاضی بنانا اُسی وقت جائز ہوگا جب کہ اس میں شہادت کی تمام شرطیں موجود ہوں ۔ مثلاً مسلمان ہو ، بالغ ہو ، عاقل ہو ، آزاد ہو اور نا بینا اور محدود فی القذف نہ ہو۔ اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ عادل ہو، عفیف ہو ، عالم بالسنہ ہو اور اپنے سے پہلے قاضیوں کے طریق پر ہو۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ جس کو عہدہ قضاء سپرد کیا جا رہا ہے وہ اہل اجتہاد میں سے ہو ۔ حاصل یہ کہ قاضی کے واسطے شہادت اور اجتہاد کا اہل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ قاضی کے اندر شہادت کی شرطوں کا پایا جانا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ حکم قضاء حکم شہادت سے مستفاد ہے۔ کیونکہ قضاء اور شہادت دونوں باب ولایت سے ہیں ۔ اور ولایت کہتے ہیں تحفیظ القول علی الغیر ۔ پس جس طرح شاہد اپنا قول غیر پر نافذ کرتا ہے اسی طرح قاضی بھی اپنا قول غیر پر نافذ کرتا ہے۔اور ولایت قضا ولایت شہادت سے چونکہ عام اور اکمل ہے۔ اس لئے ولایت قضا کے واسطے شرائط شہادت کا ہونا بدرجہ اولی ضروری ہے اور جو شخص شہادت کا اہل ہوگا وہ قاضی بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور اہلیت شہادت کے واسطے جو چیزیں شرط ہیں اہلیت قضا کے لئے بھی شرط ہوں گی ۔ پس فاسق چونکہ شہادت کا اہل ہے اسلئے وہ قاضی بننے کا بھی اہل ہوگا۔ حتی کہ فاسق کو قاضی بنا دیا گیا تو جائز ہے لیکن اس کو قاضی بنا نا مناسب نہیں ہے جیسا کہ قاضی کے لئے فاسق کی گواہی قبول کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر فاسق کی گواہی قبول کر لی گئی تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ عدالت شرائط شہادت میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ شہادت کے مناسبات میں سے ہے۔ اور اگر قاضی عادل ہو لیکن رشوت لینے یا ، شراب پینے یا زنا وغیرہ کی وجہ سے فاسق ہو گیا تو معزول نہ ہو گا۔ البتہ معزولی کا مستحق ہو جائے گا ۔ اور جب تک معزول نہیں کیا جائے گا اس وقت تک اس کے جاری کردہ احکام نافذ ہوں گے ۔ ہاں اگر قاضی مقرر کرتے وقت بادشاہ نے شرط لگا دی ہو کہ فعل حرام کا ارتکاب کرنے سے معزول ہے تو فعل حرام کا ارتکاب کرنے سے معزول ہو جائے گا۔ یہی ظاہر مذہب ہے اور اسی پر ہمارے عام مشائخ کا اعتماد ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ فاسق آدمی کو قاضی بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ ان کے نزدیک اس کی شہادت قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ یہی امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول ہے۔ اور ہمارے علماء ثلاثہ سے نوادر کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے کہ فاسق کو قاضی بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ اگر فاسق کو قاضی بنایا گیا تو درست ہے۔ اور اگر عادل کو قاضی بنایا گیا لیکن پھر وہ فاسق ہو گیا تو فسق کی وجہ سے معزول ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قاضی بنانے والے نے اس قاضی بنانے کے سلسلہ میں اس کی عدالت پر اعتماد کیا تھا۔ لہذا بغیر عدالت کے اس کو قاضی بنانے پر راضی نہ ہوگا۔ گویا قاضی بنانا بقائے عدالت کے ساتھ مشروط ہوا۔ اور جب قاضی بنانا بقائے عدالت کے ساتھ مشروط ہوا تو عدالت کے فوت ہونے سے عہدہ قضاء بھی فوت ہو جائے گا۔ بعض مشائخ کے اس قول پر ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ فقہاء کا مسلمہ قاعدہ ہے کہ بقا ابتدا کے مقابلے میں آسان اور سہل ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے نکاح بغیر گواہوں کے باقی تو رہتا ہے لیکن ابتداء درست نہیں ہوتا۔ لیکن فاسق کو قاضی بنانے کا جائز ہونا اور عادل کو اگر قاضی بنایا گیا اور پھر وہ فاسق ہو گیا تو اس فسق طاری کی وجہ سے اس کا معزول ہونا اس قاعدہ کے منافی ہے؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں قاضی بنانا عدالت پر معلق تھا اور قضاء اور امارات کو شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز بھی ہے۔ جیسا کہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک لشکر بھیجا اور ان پر زید بن حارث کو امیر بنایا اور پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ ان قتل زيد فجعفر اميركم وان قتل جعفر فعبد الله بن رواحه اميركم. یعنی اگر زید قتل کر دیا گیا تو جعفر تمہارا امیر ہے۔ اور اگر جعفر قتل کر دیا گیا تو عبد اللہ بن رواحہ تمہارا امیر ہے۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے جعفر کی امارت زید کے قتل پر معلق ہے اور عبد اللہ بن رواحہ کی امارت جعفر کے قتل پر معلق ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ قضاء اور امارت کو شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور مسئلہ مذکورہ میں قضاء عدالت پر معلق ہے اور چونکہ معلق علیہ کے فوت ہونے سے شئی معلق فوت ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے عدالت کے فوت ہونے سے قضاء کا عہدہ فوت ہو جائے گا یعنی قاضی معزول ہو جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ سوالیہ انداز میں فرماتے ہیں کہ فاسق آدمی مفتی ہو سکتا ہے یا نہیں ؟ بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ فاسق آدمی مفتی نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ کیونکہ افتاء ایک دینی امر ہے اور امور دینیہ میں فاسق کی خبر مقبول نہیں ہوتی ۔ چنانچہ اگر فاسقوں نے کہا کہ ہم نے عید کا چاند دیکھا تو ان کے قول پر اعتماد نہ ہو گا۔ اور بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فاسق آدمی کا مفتی ہونا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ لوگوں میں بدنام ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ اس کی کوشش کرے گا کہ فتویٰ صحیح لکھے اور غلطی کی طرف منسوب ہونے سے ڈرے گا۔
قاضی کیلئے اہلیت اجتہاد کی شرط کا حکم
واما الثانى فالصحيح ان اهلية الاجتهاد شرط الاولوية فاما تقليد الجاهل فصحيح عندنا خلافا للشافعي رحمة الله عليه وهو يقول ان الأمر بالقضاء يستدعى القدرة عليه ولا قدرة دون العلم ولنا انه يمكنه ان يقضى بفتوى غيره مقصود القضاء يحصل به وهو ايصال الحق الى مستحقه وينبغى للمقلد ان يختار من هو الاقدر والاولى لقوله عليه السلام من قلد انساناً عملاً و فى رعيته من هو اولى منه فقد خان الله ورسوله و جماعة المسلمين و في حد الاجتهاد كلام عرف فى اصول الفقه حاصله ان يكون صاحب حديث له معرفة
The book of the conduct of the judge. And he is just, he is removed due to sin because the appointing authority relied on his justice, so he was not satisfied with his appointment without it. And can the sinful person be a mufti? It was said no, because it is from religious matters and his report is not accepted in religious matters. And it was said he is suitable, because the sinful person strives, guarded against attribution to error. Translation: Sahib al-Quduri said that appointing a judge is not done unless the one appointed has all the conditions of testimony and he is among the people of ijtihad. Anyway, first because the ruling of judgment is derived from the ruling of testimony, because both are from the category of authority. So whoever is qualified for testimony will be qualified for judgment. And whatever is a condition for qualification of testimony is also a condition for qualification of judgment. And the sinful person is qualified for judgment, even if he is appointed as a judge it is valid, but appointing a sinful person as a judge is not appropriate, just as in the case of testimony. Because it is not appropriate for a judge to accept the testimony of a sinful person. And if the testimony of a sinful person is accepted, it is permissible in our view. And if a judge is just but becomes sinful due to bribery or other reasons, he is not removed but deserves removal. And this is the zahir al-madhhab and our mashayikh rely on it. And according to Imam Shafi'i, his testimony is not accepted. And from our three imams there is a nawadir narration that the judgment of a sinful person is not permissible. And some mashayikh said: When a sinful person is initially appointed as a judge, it is valid. And if he is appointed as a judge while just, then he becomes sinful, he will be removed due to sin, because the appointing authority relied on his justice, so he would not be satisfied with appointing him without justice. "Okay, can a sinful person be a mufti? It was said no, because giving fatwa is from religious matters and the report of a sinful person is not accepted in religious matters. And it was said that a sinful person being a mufti is valid, because fearing attribution to error, the sinful person will strive." Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that it is only permissible to appoint a person as a judge when all the conditions of testimony exist in him, for example, Muslim, adult, sane, free, not blind and not hadd for qadhf. And it is better that he be just, chaste, knowledgeable in the sunnah, and follow the way of previous judges. Second, the one entrusted with the position of judgment must be among the people of ijtihad. The summary is that for a judge, being qualified for testimony and ijtihad is necessary. The existence of the conditions of testimony in the judge is necessary because the ruling of judgment is derived from the ruling of testimony, because both judgment and testimony are from the category of authority. And authority is called enforcing one's statement upon others. So just as a witness enforces his statement upon others, similarly a judge enforces his statement upon others. And since the authority of judgment is more general and complete than the authority of testimony, so for the authority of judgment, it is a fortiori necessary that the conditions of testimony exist. And whoever is qualified for testimony can also be a judge. And whatever things are conditions for qualification of testimony will also be conditions for qualification of judgment. So the sinful person, since he is qualified for testimony, will also be qualified to become a judge. Even if a sinful person is appointed as a judge, it is permissible, but it is not appropriate to appoint him as a judge, just as it is not appropriate for a judge to accept the testimony of a sinful person. But if the testimony of a sinful person is accepted, in our view it is permissible, because justice is not among the conditions of testimony but among the proprieties of testimony. And if a judge is just but becomes sinful due to taking bribes, drinking wine, or adultery, he will not be removed; rather he becomes deserving of removal. And as long as he is not removed, his issued rulings will be effective. Yes, if at the time of appointment the king stipulated that commission of a prohibited act results in removal, then upon commission of a prohibited act he will be removed. This is the zahir al-madhhab and upon this our general mashayikh rely. Hadrat Imam Shafi'i said that appointing a sinful person as a judge is not permissible, just as in his view his testimony is not accepted. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. And from our three imams there is a nawadir narration that appointing a sinful person as a judge is not permissible. And some mashayikh said: If a sinful person is appointed as a judge, it is valid. And if a just person is appointed as a judge but then he becomes sinful, he will be removed due to sin, because the appointing authority relied on his justice in this matter of appointment; therefore he would not be satisfied with appointing him without justice. Thus the appointment was conditioned upon the continuation of justice. And when the appointment is conditioned upon the continuation of justice, then upon the loss of justice, the office of judgment will also be lost. There is an objection to this saying of some mashayikh: the established principle of the jurists is that continuation is easier and simpler than initiation. For example, marriage without witnesses remains valid but initiation is not correct. So is it contradictory that it is permissible to appoint a sinful person as a judge, but if a just person is appointed and then becomes sinful, he is removed due to this supervening sin? The answer is that in this case, the appointment of the judge was suspended on justice, and it is permissible to suspend judgment and leadership on a condition. As it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) sent an army and appointed Zayd ibn Harithah as their commander, then said: 'If Zayd is killed, Ja'far is your commander; and if Ja'far is killed, Abdullah ibn Rawahah is your commander.' Observe: the commandership of Ja'far was suspended on the killing of Zayd, and the commandership of Abdullah ibn Rawahah was suspended on the killing of Ja'far. So it is known that it is permissible to suspend judgment and leadership on a condition. And in the mentioned case, judgment is suspended on justice. And since the suspended thing is lost upon the loss of the condition, therefore upon the loss of justice, the office of judgment is lost, meaning the judge is removed. The author of Hidayah asks in a questioning manner: Can a sinful person be a mufti or not? Some scholars are of the opinion that a sinful person cannot be a mufti, because ifta is a religious matter and in religious matters the report of a sinful person is not accepted. For instance, if sinful people say that they have seen the moon of Eid, their statement will not be relied upon. And some scholars are of the opinion that a sinful person being a mufti is permissible, because due to being notorious among people, he will strive to write a correct fatwa and will fear being attributed to error. The ruling on the condition of ijtihad for a judge: As for the second, the correct view is that the qualification of ijtihad is a condition of preference. As for the taqlid of a ignorant person, it is valid in our view, contrary to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. He says that the command of judgment requires ability upon it, and there is no ability without knowledge. And our evidence is that it is possible for him to judge by the fatwa of someone else; the purpose of judgment is achieved by it, which is delivering the right to its owner. And it is befitting for one who does taqlid to choose the most capable and preferable, due to his saying (ﷺ): 'Whoever appoints a person over a work while among his subjects there is one more capable than him, has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the community of Muslims.' And regarding the definition of ijtihad, there is discussion known in usul al-fiqh; its summary is that he should be a scholar of hadith with knowledge.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the qualifications of a judge (qadi) and a mufti, focusing on the effect of sinfulness (fisq). The author begins by stating a general principle: a judge who is just but becomes sinful is not automatically removed from office, contrary to the view of some that he is. The reason is that the appointing authority (ruler) relied on his justice at the time of appointment, so the ruler was not satisfied with appointing him without justice. However, the passage then addresses whether a sinful person can be a mufti. Two opinions are presented: one rejects it because a sinful person's report is not accepted in religious matters, and the other accepts it because the sinful person will be extra cautious due to fear of being accused of error.

The commentary by the translator (mufassir) further explains the conditions for appointing a qadi: he must have all the conditions of a witness (Muslim, adult, sane, free, not blind, not punished for false accusation) and preferably be just, chaste, knowledgeable in sunnah, and follow the ways of previous judges. Additionally, he must be qualified for ijtihad. The reason for requiring the conditions of testimony is that judgment is a form of authority (wilayah) like testimony, and since judgment is more comprehensive, it requires those conditions a fortiori.

Regarding the sinful person, since he is qualified to give testimony (according to the Hanafi view, justice is not a condition for testimony but a recommendatio), he is also qualified to be a judge. Appointing a fasiq as judge is valid but not preferred, just as accepting his testimony is valid but not preferred. If a just judge becomes sinful, he is not automatically removed unless the ruler stipulated that condition at the time of appointment. This is the relied-upon position (zahir al-madhhab).

The passage then contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, who hold that a fasiq cannot be a judge, analogous to his testimony being rejected. It also mentions a nawadir narration from the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) that a fasiq's judgment is invalid.

Some later mashayikh made a distinction: if a fasiq is initially appointed, it is valid; but if a just person is appointed and then becomes fasiq, he is removed because the appointment was conditioned on his justice. This view is critiqued with the principle that continuation is easier than initiation, but defended by showing that appointment can be suspended on a condition, as in the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) suspending command on the death of a commander.

Finally, the passage discusses the requirement of ijtihad for a qadi. The correct view is that ijtihad is a condition of preference (shart al-awlawiyyah), not validity. Therefore, a qadi who follows another (muqallid) can validly judge based on the fatwa of a mujtahid, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who requires ijtihad for validity. The Hanafi proof is that the purpose of judgment (delivering rights) can be achieved through the fatwa of another, and the ruling in favor of the muqallid is supported by the hadith condemning appointment of a less qualified person.

Key Terms
عدالت (adalat): Justice; moral rectitude; freedom from fisq. In this text, it is discussed as a condition for the preference of a qadi, not for validity.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness; commission of major sins or persistence in minor sins. A fasiq is someone who has abandoned justice.
ولایت (wilayah): Authority; the power to enforce one's statement upon others. Both judgment (qada) and testimony (shahadah) are forms of wilayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a just judge becomes sinful (fasiq) due to bribery, what happens to his position?
A) He is immediately removed from office.
B) He remains in office and his rulings are valid; he deserves removal but is not automatically removed unless stipulated.
C) He remains in office but his rulings become invalid.
D) He is removed only if he commits a hadd offense.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a fasiq can be a valid qadi, but it is not preferred; automatic removal is not the relied-upon view.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
Ijtihad as a Condition of Preference for the Qadi
Commentary on the requirement of ijtihad for a qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ijtihad is a condition of preference (shart al-awlawiyyah) for a qadi in the Hanafi school and distinguish this from the Shafi'i view that it is a condition of validity.

Core Idea
A muqallid qadi is valid: ijtihad is a condition of preference, not validity.

This lesson addresses the requirement of ijtihad for a judge. The Hanafi school holds that a judge who is a muqallid (follower) can validly adjudicate by relying on the fatwa of a mujtahid, whereas the Shafi'i school requires ijtihad for validity. We'll examine the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on ijtihad for a qadi
Hanafi: ijtihad is a condition of preference (shart al-awlawiyyah), not validity. Shafi'i: ijtihad is a condition of validity (shart al-sihhah).
2
State the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that a muqallid qadi can judge by the fatwa of a mujtahid; the purpose of judgment (delivering rights) is achieved. The hadith about appointing a less capable person shows blameworthiness but not invalidity.
The hadith: 'Whoever appoints a person over a work while among his subjects there is one more capable than him, has betrayed Allah...'
3
State the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the command of judgment (al-amr bi al-qada) requires ability (qudrah), and without knowledge (ilm) there is no ability. A muqallid lacks the knowledge to derive rulings.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: ability can be achieved through the fatwa of another; the judge's role is to enforce, not necessarily to derive. The hadith indicates blame but not nullity.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Shafi'i practice, a muqallid cannot be appointed as qadi; in Hanafi, he can, though it is preferable to appoint a mujtahid.
