امام محمد کو قضاء کا عہدہ پیش کیا گیا تو امام محمد نے بھی انکار فرمایا حتی کہ امام موصوف کو قید خانہ میں ڈال دیا گیا تو مجبورا قبول کرنا پڑا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسیح قول یہ ہے کہ عدل و انصاف قائم کرنے کے ارادہ سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے یعنی اگر قاضی ہو گیا تو گنہگار نہ ہو گا۔ لیکن عزیمت اس کو ترک کرنا ہے۔ اور اسکی نظیر موزوں پر مسح اور سفر میں روزہ ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح موزوں پر مسح کرنا رخصت اور پاؤں دھونا عزیمت ہے۔ اور سفر میں افطار رخصت اور روزہ رکھنا عزیمت ہے۔ اسی طرح عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا رخصت اور
For whom accepting judgeship is disliked: He said: ‘And it is disliked to enter upon it for one who fears inability and does not feel secure from injustice in it, so that it does not become a condition for committing evil. And some disliked entering upon it absolutely, choosing the saying of peace be upon him: “Whoever is appointed to judgeship has been slaughtered without a knife.” And the correct view is that entering upon it is a concession (rukhsah) in hope of establishing justice, and leaving it is the more cautious (azima). For perhaps his assumption may be mistaken and he may not be granted success, or no one else may assist him, and assistance is necessary. Except when he himself is the only qualified person for judgeship, then it becomes obligatory upon him to undertake it to safeguard the rights of people and rid the world of corruption.’ Translation: And for one who fears inability and is not secure from injustice, it is disliked (makruh tahrimi) so that acceptance does not become a means to evil. Some scholars deemed it absolutely disliked based on the hadith. The correct view is that it is a concession for those who intend justice, and leaving it is more cautious. The analogy is drawn to wiping over socks (khuffs) which is a rukhsah versus washing the feet (azima), and breaking fast in travel (rukhsah) versus fasting (azima). Thus, judgeship is permissible but avoiding it is better unless no one else is qualified, in which case it becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on judgeship, now focusing on when it is disliked. Al-Quduri states: 'It is disliked (yukrah) for one who fears inability and does not feel secure from falling into injustice.' The reason is to prevent such a person from committing evil. Then it mentions that some scholars deemed it absolutely disliked in all cases, citing the Prophet's hadith: 'Whoever is appointed as a judge is slaughtered without a knife.' However, the correct view according to the commentator is that entering into judgeship is a rukhsah (allowance) for those who seek to establish justice, while avoiding it is the 'azima (more cautious path). The hadith is interpreted as a warning against the responsibility, not as a prohibition. The text further explains that if a person is the only one qualified for judgeship, then it becomes obligatory (fard 'ayn) on him to accept in order to protect the rights of people. The commentator draws an analogy to wiping over khuffs (allowed but not preferred) and breaking fast in travel (allowed but fasting is more virtuous). This illustrates that judgeship is permissible for the confident and capable, but the more cautious choice is to avoid it if not needed.

Key Terms
کراہت تحریمی (karāhat taḥrīmiyya): Prohibitively disliked; close to haram. Here it means it is sinful for the one who fears inability to accept.
رخصت (rukhṣat): A concession; an allowance that eases the original ruling due to necessity or valid reason.
عزیمت (ʿazīmat): The original, more cautious ruling; the higher path preferred in the absence of necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who fears he cannot judge justly?
A) Permissible
B) Obligatory
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the capable judge (permissible) and the one who fears injustice (makruh tahrimi), with the possibility of obligation if no one else qualifies.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Ruling on Accepting Judgeship: Concession or Obligation
Ruling on accepting judgeship: distinguishing concession from determination and the exception of unique qualification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting judgeship and identify the conditions under which it becomes permissible, disliked, or obligatory.

Core Idea
Accepting judgeship is permissible as a concession, but leaving it is the stronger resolve—unless you are uniquely needed.

This lesson addresses the legal ruling on accepting the position of a judge (qadha) within the Hanafi school. The classical texts present a spectrum of opinions, from absolute dislike to obligation, depending on the individual's qualifications and intention. We will explore the correct view as stated in Al-Hidayah, the evidence from the hadith of Abu Hurairah, and the key distinction between concession (rukhsah) and determination (azimah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act (accepting judgeship)? What are the possible rulings? The passage presents three: ja'iz (permissible), makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and fard (obligatory). The correct view is that it is ja'iz as a concession.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'Whoever is placed in charge of judging is as if slaughtered without a knife.' This hadith is used by those who hold it disliked.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and zanni al-dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith's comparison indicates the great responsibility and potential for sin. The correct interpretation is that it warns against entering without proper qualifications, not that it prohibits absolutely.
The analogy with wiping socks and travel fasting illustrates that a concession can coexist with a stronger path.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Al-Quduri and others hold it as makruh tahrimi conditionally or absolutely. The correct view in Al-Hidayah is that it is ja'iz for one who intends justice, but leaving is azimah.
The ikhtilaf is resolved by Sahib al-Hidayah, who declares his view as the sahih qawl.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that accepting judgeship is ja'iz as a rukhsah when one is confident and intends justice. However, if the person is uniquely qualified and no one else can fulfill the role, it becomes fard.
The tarjih is based on the need to preserve rights and prevent corruption.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد نہم القبيح وكره بعضهم الدخول فيه مختار القوله عليه السلام من جعل على القضا فكانما ذبح بغير سكين والصحيح ان الدخول فيه رخصة طمعاً فى اقامة العدل والترك عزيمة فلعله يخطى ظنه ولا يوفق له اولا يعينه علیه غيره ولا بد من الاعانة الا اذا كان هو الاهل للقضاء دون غيره فحينئذ يفترض عليه التقلد صيانة لحقوق العباد واخلاء للعالم عن الفساد
ترجمہ اور جو شخص قضاء بالحق سے عاجزی کا خوف رکھتا ہو اور اپنی ذات پر حکم قضا میں ظلم سے مطمئن نہ ہو تو اس کو قضاء میں داخل ہونا مکروہ ہے تا کہ یہ داخل ہونا اس کے امر قبیح کے مرتکب ہونے کا وسیلہ نہ ہو۔ اور بعض علماء نے مطلقاً عہدہ قضاء میں داخل ہونا مکروہ قرار دیا ہے۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کہ جو شخص قضاء پر مقرر کیا گیا گویا وہ بغیر چھری کے ذبح کیا گیا، کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ عدل قائم کرنے کی طمع میں قضاء میں داخل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔ اور اس کو چھوڑ دینا عزیمت ہے۔ کیونک ممکن ہے کہ اس کا گمان خطاء کرے اور اس کو درستگی کی توفیق نہ ہو۔ یا قاضی کی حکم قضا پر دوسرا شخص اعانت نہ کرے حالانکہ اعانت ضروری ہے مگر جب قضاء کا اہل یہی ہو نہ کہ دوسرا کوئی شخص تو اس وقت اس پر عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا فرض ہے تا کہ بندوں کے حقوق کی حفاظت کرے اور عالم کو فساد سے خالی کرے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر کسی شخص کو قضاء بالحق سے بجز کا اندیشہ ہو ۔ اور ظلم اور بے انصافی سے اپنی ذات پر مطمئن نہ ہو تو ایسے شخص کے لئے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا مکروہ تحریمی ہے تا کہ قضاء کا عہدہ قبول کرنا امر قبیح یعنی ظلم اور بے انصافی کے ارتکاب کا وسیلہ نہ ہو۔ اور بعض علماء کے نزدیک عہدہ قضاء کا قبول کرنا مطلقاً مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔ خواہ اپنے اوپر اعتماد کرے یا خوف کرے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ یہاں کراہت سے مراد عدم جواز ہے اور دلیل میں یہ فرمایا کہ صدر الشہید نے ادب القاضی میں کہا ہے ومنهم من قال لا يجوز الدخول فيه الامكرها بعض علماء نے فرمایا کہ عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر زبر دستی یعنی اگر زبر دستی پیش کیا جائے تو جائز ہے۔

امام محمد کو قضاء کا عہدہ پیش کیا گیا تو امام محمد نے بھی انکار فرمایا حتی کہ امام موصوف کو قید خانہ میں ڈال دیا گیا تو مجبورا قبول کرنا پڑا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ عدل و انصاف قائم کرنے کے ارادہ سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے یعنی اگر قاضی ہو گیا تو گنہگار نہ ہو گا۔ لیکن عزیمت اس کو ترک کرنا ہے۔ اور اس کی نظیر موزوں پر مسح اور سفر میں روزہ ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح موزوں پر مسح کرنا رخصت اور پاؤں دھونا عزیمت ہے۔ اور سفر میں افطار رخصت اور روزہ رکھنا عزیمت ہے۔ اسی طرح عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا رخصت اور
كتاب الادب القاضي
۲۵۲
اشرف البدایہ جلد نهم ترک کرنا عزیمت ہے۔ ترکہ کے عزیمت ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی اگر مجتہد نہ ہو تو اس کا امکان ہے کہ وہ غلطی کر جائے اور اس کو صحیح فیصلہ کی توفیق نہ ہو یا قاضی خود مجتہد نہ ہو۔ اور دوسرا آدمی اس کی اعانت نہ کرے حالانکہ اس صورت میں اعانت ضروری ہے۔ پس ان حالات کے پیش نظر ترک کرنا ہی عزیمت ہے۔ ہاں اگر قاضی ہونے کے لائق یہی شخص ہو اور دوسرا کوئی موجود نہ ہو تو ایسی صورت میں عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا فرض ہے۔ تا کہ بندوں کے حقوق کی حفاظت کرے اور عالم کو فساد ظلم سے خالی کرے۔
Book of the Conduct of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume nine. 'The undesirable, and some of them disliked entering into it, and the chosen (position) is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): "Whoever is placed in charge of judging is as if he is slaughtered without a knife." And the correct (view) is that entering into it is a concession out of desire to establish justice, and leaving it is determination, because perhaps his guess will be wrong and he will not be granted success, or no one else will help him, while assistance is necessary, unless he is the one qualified for judging without anyone else, then the position becomes obligatory upon him to preserve the rights of the people and to free the world from corruption.' Translation: 'And a person who fears inability regarding judging with truth and is not confident about himself regarding justice in judgment, then entering into judging is disliked for him, so that this entering does not become a means for him to commit an undesirable act. And some scholars consider entering the position of judge absolutely disliked, because they adopt the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that whoever is appointed as judge is as if slaughtered without a knife. And the correct saying is that entering into judging is permitted out of desire to establish justice, and leaving it is determination (azimah). Because it is possible that his guess is wrong and he is not granted correctness, or another person does not assist him in the judgment, while assistance is necessary, but when he is the one qualified for judging and no one else, then at that time accepting the position of judge is obligatory upon him to protect the rights of the people and to free the world from corruption.' Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that if a person fears inability regarding judging with truth and is not confident about himself regarding injustice and unfairness, then for such a person accepting the position of judge is makruh tahrimi, so that accepting the position does not become a means for committing an undesirable act, i.e., injustice and unfairness. And according to some scholars, accepting the position of judge is absolutely makruh tahrimi, whether one relies on himself or fears. Sahib al-Inayah wrote that here 'karahah' means lack of permissibility, and as evidence, he said that Sadr al-Shahid said in Adab al-Qadi: 'And among them are those who said it is not permissible to enter into it unless forced.' Some scholars said that accepting the position of judge is not permissible unless by coercion, i.e., if forced, then it is permissible. Their evidence is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that whoever is appointed as judge is as if slaughtered without a knife. The comparison of the position of judge to slaughter without a knife is because a knife is effective both outwardly and inwardly, while slaughter without a knife is effective inwardly due to the soul leaving but not outwardly. Similarly, the position of judge is not effective outwardly but is effective inwardly, because outwardly it is a great office but inwardly it is pure destruction. This is why Imam Abu Hanifah was offered the position of judge three times and refused each time, and for his refusal, he was given three lashes each time. Similarly, Imam Muhammad was offered the position of judge and also refused until he was imprisoned and had to accept under compulsion. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the correct saying is that accepting the position of judge with the intention of establishing justice is permissible, i.e., if he becomes judge, he will not be sinful. But determination (azimah) is to leave it. Its analogy is wiping over socks and fasting in travel: just as wiping over socks is a concession and washing the feet is determination, and breaking the fast in travel is a concession and fasting is determination, similarly accepting the position of judge is a concession and leaving it is determination. The evidence that leaving is determination is that if the judge is not a mujtahid, it is possible that he makes a mistake and is not granted correctness, or he is not a mujtahid himself, and another person does not assist him, while assistance is necessary in this case. So in these circumstances, leaving is determination. Yes, if this person is the only one qualified to be judge and no one else exists, then in that case accepting the position of judge is obligatory, so that he protects the rights of the people and frees the world from the corruption of injustice.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the acceptance of the position of a judge (qadha). It begins with the base text (matn) stating that entering into judgeship is disliked by some, and then presents the correct view: it is a concession (rukhsah) when the intention is to establish justice, but leaving it is the stronger resolve (azimah). The author then provides the proof, the hadith: 'Whoever is placed in charge of judging is as if he is slaughtered without a knife,' and explains that the correct position is that it is a concession. The passage then makes a crucial distinction: if a person fears that he may be unable to judge with truth and is not confident in his own justice, then accepting the position becomes makruh tahrimi for him. However, if he is uniquely qualified and no one else can fulfill the role, it becomes obligatory (fard) upon him to accept the position to protect the rights of the people and prevent corruption in the world. The commentary (sharh) then elaborates on these points, citing Al-Quduri, Al-Inayah, and Sadr al-Shahid, and provides the example of Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani refusing the position, showing the strength of the azimah. The author, Sahib al-Hidayah, analogizes this to the concession of wiping over socks in wudu and breaking the fast in travel, both of which are concessions compared to the azimah of washing the feet and fasting. The key takeaway is that while accepting judgeship is generally permissible (ja'iz), the safer and more deserving path is to avoid it unless one is compelled or uniquely needed.

Key Terms
تقلد القضاء (taqallud al-qadha): Accepting the position of a judge or being appointed to the judiciary.
رخصة (rukhsah): A dispensation or concession that allows something that would normally be restricted, due to a valid excuse.
عزيمة (azimah): The original, stricter ruling that is followed when there is no excuse; the preferred path.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): A disliked act that is closer to haram; one should avoid it, and repeating it is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in Al-Hidayah, what is the ruling on accepting the position of a judge for a person who intends to establish justice but is not uniquely qualified?
A) It is haram (forbidden)
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
C) It is ja'iz (permissible) but leaving it is azimah (better)
D) It is fard (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
Accepting judgeship is a contextual ruling: permissible with right intention, disliked when fearing injustice, and obligatory when uniquely needed; the stronger path is to avoid it unless compelled.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Seeking the Position of Judge
Ruling with proof from hadith and rational argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on actively seeking a judgeship and explain the proof from the hadith and rational reasoning.

Core Idea
Seeking a judgeship deprives one of divine help; accepting when forced brings angelic support.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling in Islamic governance: whether one may actively seek the position of a judge. The text presents both scriptural and rational evidence that seeking is discouraged, while accepting under compulsion is permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is actively seeking or requesting the position of a judge (talab al-qadha). The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibited) according to the stronger view.
The matn uses 'yanbaghi an la yatalaba' indicating it is not appropriate to seek.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever seeks judging is entrusted to his own self, and whoever is forced upon it, an angel descends upon him that keeps him straight.' This is a hadith reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The first part of the hadith directly links seeking to being left to one's own self (deprivation of divine help). This implies that seeking leads to harm, hence prohibition. The second part shows that compulsion brings angelic assistance, indicating that it is the compulsion that brings blessing, not seeking.
The phrase 'yufawwad ila nafsihi' indicates being deprived of tawfiq.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
While the Hanafi school holds it as makruh tahrimi, some later scholars considered it merely makruh tanzihi. The Shafi'i school also discourages seeking but some permit it if one is capable and intends justice.
The text sides with the stronger view based on the hadith and rational proof.
5
Apply the ruling to related scenarios
The ruling applies only to actively seeking. If the position is offered without solicitation, it is permissible to accept. The rational proof explains that seeking shows self-reliance, while compulsion leads to tawakkul.
The verse 'Indeed, the soul is a persistent enjoiner of evil' (12:53) supports the danger of self-reliance.

Source Text

عہدہ قضاء طلب کرنے کا حکم
قال وينبغى ان لا يطلب الولاية ولا يسألها لقوله عليه السلام من طلب القضاوكل الى نفسه ومن اجبر عليه نزل عليه ملک يسدده ولان من طلبه يعتمد على نفسه فيحرم ومن اجبر عليه يتوكل على ربه فيلهم
ترجمہ : اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ آدمی نہ ولایت تلاش کرے اور نہ اس کی درخواست کرے۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس شخص نے عہدہ قضاء طلب کیا تو اس کو اُس کے نفس کے سپرد کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور جس کو عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا گیا اُس پر ایک فرشتہ نازل ہوتا ہے جو اس کو درست رکھتا ہے اور اس لئے کہ جس نے عہدہ قضاء کو طلب کیا وہ اپنے نفس پر اعتماد کرتا ہے۔ پس وہ محروم کیا جاتا ہے اور جس کو اس پر مجبور کیا گیا وہ اپنے رب پر بھروسہ کرتا ہے پس اس کو الہام کیا جاتا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی شخص قاضی ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو تب بھی اس کو چاہئے کہ نہ تو وہ دل سے اس کی خواہش کرے اور نہ زبان سے اس کی درخواست کرے۔ کیونکہ حضرت انس کی حدیث ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس شخص نے عہدہ قضاء طلب کیا اس کو اس کے نفس کے سپرد کر دیا گیا اور جس کو اُس پر مجبور کیا گیا اُس پر ایک فرشتہ اترتا ہے۔ جو اس کو راہ راست پر رکھتا ہے۔
عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو شخص عہدہ کا طالب ہے گویا اس نے اپنے فہم ، ورع اور ذکاوت پر بھروسہ کیا اور ان چیزوں پر بھروسہ کرنے کی وجہ سے عجب اور کبر میں مبتلا ہو گیا اور جوشخص معجب اور کبر کی وجہ سے اپنے نفس پر بھروسہ کرتا ہے وہ توفیق الہی سے محروم رہتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے ان النفس لامارة بالسوء اور جو عہد قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا گیا وہ اپنے پروردگار پر بھروسہ کرتا ہے۔ اور جو اللہ پر بھروسہ کرتا ہے اس کو توفیق الہی سے نوازا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے عہدہ کا طلب نہ کرنا مناسب ہے۔ اور اگر بزرگوں کی طرف سے دیدیا جائے تو قبول کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ بھی نہیں ہے۔
Ruling on seeking the position of judge. He said: 'It is appropriate that one should not seek governorship nor ask for it, because of his saying (peace be upon him): "Whoever seeks judging is entrusted to himself, and whoever is forced upon it, an angel descends upon him that keeps him straight." And because the one who seeks it relies on himself, so he is deprived, and the one who is forced upon it relies on his Lord, so he is inspired.' Translation: 'And it is appropriate that a person should neither seek governorship nor request it. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever seeks the position of judge is entrusted to his own self, and whoever is forced to accept it, an angel descends upon him that keeps him correct." And because the one who seeks it relies on his own self, so he is deprived, and the one who is forced upon it relies on his Lord, so he is inspired.' Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that even if a person is capable of being a judge, he should neither desire it in his heart nor request it by tongue, because of the hadith of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever seeks the position of judge is entrusted to his own self, and whoever is forced upon it, an angel descends upon him that keeps him on the straight path.' The rational proof is that the one who seeks the position has relied on his understanding, piety, and intelligence, and due to reliance on these things, he falls into self-admiration and arrogance. And a person who, due to self-admiration and arrogance, relies on his own self is deprived of divine success. Because Allah Almighty says: 'Indeed, the soul is a persistent enjoiner of evil.' And the one who is forced to accept the position relies on his Lord. And whoever relies on Allah is granted divine success. Therefore, it is appropriate not to seek the position. But if it is given by the authorities, there is no harm in accepting it.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof on seeking the position of a judge. The base matn states that one should not seek or ask for the position of governorship or judgeship. The proof is the hadith that whoever seeks judgeship is left to his own devices (and thus deprived of divine help), while whoever is forced into it has an angel descend to keep him straight. The commentary (sharh) by Al-Quduri emphasizes that even a qualified person should not desire it internally or request it verbally. A rational proof (dalil aqli) is added: seeking it shows reliance on oneself, leading to self-admiration (ujb) and arrogance (kibr), which cuts one off from divine success. The verse 'Indeed, the soul is a persistent enjoiner of evil' (Quran 12:53) supports that relying on one's self is dangerous. However, if the position is offered by the authorities (e.g., a ruler or senior scholars), accepting it is permissible and not problematic. This shows the balance: avoiding ambition for power but accepting responsibility when imposed.

Key Terms
طلب القضاء (talab al-qadha): Actively seeking or requesting the position of a judge.
توكّل (tawakkul): Trust in Allah; relying on Allah rather than oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Seeking judgeship is prohibited due to reliance on self; accepting under compulsion is permissible.

Accepting Judgeship from an Unjust Ruler
Explains that accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler is permissible, citing the practice of the Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler and apply the condition that the judge must be able to rule with truth.

Core Idea
Accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler is permissible if truth can be upheld.

Can a Muslim jurist accept a judicial appointment from a tyrant? The Hanafi school, citing the practice of the Companions and Followers, rules that it is permissible as long as the judge can rule justly. The key condition is the ability to uphold truth, not the character of the ruler.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify the act (accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler) and the ruling given by the text: it is permissible (ja'iz).
The text says 'yajuz' (it is permissible).
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The text cites the practice of the Sahaba (Companions) and the Tabieen (Followers) as proof. Specifically, the Sahaba accepted judgeship under Muawiyah, and the Tabieen under Hajjaj ibn Yusuf.
This is a form of ijma (consensus) through action.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does this practice prove permissibility? The fact that the Sahaba and Tabieen did it without denial from others indicates it is allowed. The truth (rightful caliph) was with Ali, yet they served under Muawiyah, showing that the ruler's justice is not a prerequisite.
The focus is on the judge's ability to implement justice.
4
Identify the condition
The text adds an exception: 'unless he does not enable him to judge with truth.' If the ruler prevents just rulings, then acceptance is not permissible.
The condition is based on achieving the purpose of judgeship.
5
Note the cross-madhhab position
Some scholars (e.g., some Shafi'is) hold that accepting from an unjust ruler is impermissible due to supporting tyranny. The Hanafi school prioritizes the potential for justice over the ruler's character.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different priorities.

Source Text

ثم يجوز التقلد من السلطان الجائر كما يجوز من العادل لان الصحابة تقلد و امن معاوية والحق كان بيد علي في نوبته والتابعين تقلد وأمن الحجاج وهو كان جائراً الا اذا كان لا يمكنه من القضأ بحق لان رد لا يحصل قلد بخلاف ما اذا كان يمكـ

Ruling on accepting the position of judge from an unjust ruler. Then it is permissible to accept the position from an unjust ruler just as it is permissible from a just ruler, because the Companions (Sahaba) accepted from Muawiyah, and the truth was with Ali in his time, and the Followers (Tabieen) accepted from Hajjaj, and he was unjust, unless he does not enable him to judge with truth, because then the acceptance does not achieve (the purpose). The translation: 'Then, accepting the position of judge from an unjust king is permissible just as it is permissible from a just king, because the Companions accepted from Muawiyah, and the truth was with Ali in his time, and the Followers accepted from Hajjaj, and he was unjust, unless he does not enable him to judge with truth, because then the acceptance does not achieve (justice).'
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding accepting the position of judge from an unjust ruler. The matn states that it is permissible to accept the appointment from both a just and an unjust ruler. The proof is the practice of the Sahaba: they accepted judgeship under Muawiyah (even though the rightful caliph was Ali during that period), and the Tabieen (successors) accepted under Hajjaj ibn Yusuf, who was known to be unjust. This shows that the validity of the appointment does not depend on the ruler's justice. However, there is a condition: if the unjust ruler prevents the judge from judging according to truth (i.e., interferes or forces injustice), then accepting the position is not permissible because the purpose of justice would not be achieved. The text is cut off, but the condition is clear. The underlying principle is that one should accept the position if it allows the establishment of justice, even if the ruler is unjust, because it can be a means to protect rights and reduce corruption.

Key Terms
سلطان جائر (sultan jair): An unjust or tyrannical ruler; someone who does not rule by Shariah.

Key Takeaway
Accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler is permissible in the Hanafi school as long as the judge is able to rule according to truth, based on the practice of the Sahaba and Tabieen.

Accepting Judgeship from a Tyrannical Ruler
Ruling with proof based on historical precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting judgeship from a tyrannical ruler, identify the condition, and explain the proof from the practice of the Companions and Followers.

Core Idea
Accepting judgeship from a tyrant is permissible if you can uphold justice.

This lesson examines the delicate issue of accepting a judicial appointment from an unjust ruler. The Hanafi school, known for its practical orientation, permits it under a vital condition. The ruling is derived from the actual practice of the Companions and Followers, as recorded in Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is accepting the position of judge (qadi) from a tyrannical ruler. The ruling is jaiz (permissible) but conditional.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the judge's ability to rule justly.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The primary evidence is the practice (ijma sukti) of the Companions accepting judgeship from Muawiyah and the Followers from Hajjaj. No one objected, indicating silent consensus.
Muawiyah is considered a tyrant by Ahl al-Sunnah because he rebelled against the rightful caliph Ali.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the historical precedent prove permissibility? The fact that the Companions accepted such positions without widespread condemnation shows that the act is not inherently forbidden.
The Hanafis see this as a form of istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity.
4
Identify the condition
The judge must be able to adjudicate with justice. If he cannot, the acceptance is not permissible because the purpose of judgeship (establishing justice) is thwarted.
The condition is on the judge's ability, not the ruler's character.
5
Contrast with opposing views
Some Shafi'i scholars deem it impermissible, arguing it supports tyranny. Hanafis respond by citing the Companions' practice and the benefit of enabling justice.
The difference is legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools aim to uphold justice.

تجھ کو کس چیز نے روکا کہ تو مجھ کو میرے سفر سے روکتا ؟ ابن عمر نے کہا کہ میں نے دیکھا کہ تجھ پر ایک آدمی یعنی ابن زبیر غالب آ گیا۔ پس عائشہ نے کہا کہ بخدا اگر تو مجھ کومنع کرتا تو میں نہ نکلتی ۔ یہ اس وقت کا واقعہ ہے جب حضرت عائشہ حضرت معاویہ کی حمایت میں حضرت علیؓ کے خلاف جنگ کے ارادہ سے نکلی تھیں ۔ اور پھر جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث یاد آئی تو نادم ہو کر واپس تشریف لے آئیں۔ اس پر عائشہ نے ابن عمر سے کہا کہ اگر آپ ابتدا میں مجھ کو منع کر دیتے تو میں نہ نکلتی۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ”حق“ حضرت علی کی طرف تھا۔ بہر حال ان حکایات و روایات سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہادت عثمان کے بعد خلافت کا حق حضرت علی کو تھا مگر اس کے باوجود حضرت معاویہ کا حضرت علی کے ہاتھ پر بیعت نہ کرنا۔ اور ملک شام میں اپنی حکمرانی کا اعلان کرنا کھلی ہوئی بغاوت تھی۔ پس حضرت معاویہ کا سلطان جائر ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ اور تاریخ اس پر شاہد ہے کہ حضرت معاویہؓ نے صحابہ کو قاضی مقرر فرمایا ہے۔ اور صحابہ نے حضرت معاویہ کی طرف سے عہدوں کو قبول بھی فرمایا ہے۔ جیسے: حضرت ابوالد رد آن کو شام میں قاضی مقرر فرمایا اور پھر ان کی وفات کے بعد انہی کے مشورہ کے مطابق فضالہ بن عبید انصاری کو والی شام مقرر فرمایا۔ اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ سلطان جائر کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دوسری دلیل میں فرمایا کہ حجاج بن یوسف مشہور ظالم فرمانروا گذرا ہے۔ مگر تا بعین نے اس کی طرف سے بھی قضاء کے عہدے قبول کئے ہیں۔ مثلاً : حجاج بن یوسف نے ابو بردہ ابن ابی موسیٰ کو قاضی مقرر کیا۔ اور عبد اللہ بن ابی مریم نے اصفہان کا قاضی ہونا حجاج ہی کی طرف سے قبول کیا ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ظالم بادشاہ کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ظالم بادشاہ کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے لیکن اگر قاضی کے لئے حق کے ساتھ فیصلہ کرنا ممکن نہ ہو
The ruling on accepting the position of judge from a tyrannical ruler: Then it is permissible to accept the position from a tyrannical ruler just as it is permissible from a just one, because the Companions accepted it from Muawiyah, and the truth (of caliphate) was with Ali in his time. And the Followers accepted it from Hajjaj, and he was tyrannical. Except if the judge is not able to judge with justice, because then the purpose of accepting the position is not achieved, unlike the case when he is able. Translation: Then accepting the position of judge from a tyrannical king is permissible just as it is permissible from a just king, because the Companions accepted it from Muawiyah, and the right of caliphate was in the hands of Ali. And the Followers accepted it from Hajjaj, although he was tyrannical. Except if the judge is not able to judge with justice, because then the purpose of accepting the position will not be achieved, contrary to the case when he is able. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that just as it is permissible to accept the position of judge from a just and rightful king, similarly it is permissible from a tyrannical and unrightful king. That is, if a person rebels and overcomes and becomes a ruler, then compels someone to be a judge, it is permissible to accept from him. Sahib al-Hidayah presented as evidence that after the martyrdom of Uthman, the right of caliphate was for Ali, as Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah agree. But Muawiyah rebelled against Ali and became ruler of Syria. The scholars of Al-Hidayah cited the hadith from the Prophet to Ammar ibn Yasir: 'The rebellious group will kill you,' and indeed Ammar was killed by Muawiyah's companions. This shows Muawiyah and his group were rebels. Aisha initially was with Muawiyah but later regretted. Ibn Abdul Barr narrated that Aisha said to Ibn Umar: 'O Abu Abdur Rahman, what prevented you from forbidding me from my journey?' He said: 'I saw a man overpowering you, meaning Ibn al-Zubayr.' She said: 'By Allah, if you had forbidden me, I would not have gone out.' This indicates that the truth was with Ali. These narrations establish that Muawiyah was a tyrannical ruler. History witnesses that Muawiyah appointed Companions as judges, and they accepted. For example, he appointed Abu al-Darda as judge in Syria, and after his death, Fadalah ibn Ubayd al-Ansari. This proves acceptance from a tyrant is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah gave another evidence that Hajjaj ibn Yusuf, a famous tyrant, appointed Abu Burdah ibn Abi Musa as judge, and Abdullah ibn Abi Maryam accepted judgeship of Isfahan from him. This shows it is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah says it is permissible from a tyrannical king, but if the judge is not able to judge with justice
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof based on historical precedent. It addresses the permissibility of accepting the office of judge from a tyrannical ruler. The matn states that it is permissible just as from a just ruler, and the commentary provides two proofs: (1) the Companions accepted judgeship from Muawiyah, who is considered a tyrant according to Ahl al-Sunnah because he rebelled against the rightful caliph Ali; (2) the Followers accepted from Hajjaj, a notorious tyrant. The key condition is that the judge must be able to adjudicate with justice; if he cannot, the appointment is invalid because the purpose of judgeship is to establish justice. The Hanafi position is clear: one may accept from a tyrant to prevent greater harm, but only if one can uphold justice. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) balancing the need for social order and the obligation to enforce Islamic law.

Key Terms
السلطان الجائر (al-sultan al-ja'ir): A ruler who has taken power through rebellion or injustice, not the rightful caliph.
التقلد (al-taqallud): Accepting or taking on a position, here specifically judgeship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence for the permissibility of accepting judgeship from a tyrannical ruler?
A) Quranic verse
B) Hadith
C) Practice of the Companions and Followers
D) Qiyas

Key Takeaway
Accepting judgeship from a tyrannical ruler is permissible in the Hanafi school provided the judge can adjudicate with justice, based on the silent consensus of the early community.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
Accepting Judgeship from an Unjust Ruler
Ruling on accepting judgeship from unjust ruler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler and state the condition that determines its permissibility or prohibition.

Core Idea
Accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler is permissible if the judge can rule with truth; otherwise it is forbidden.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a sensitive question: can a Muslim accept a judicial appointment from a ruler who came to power through rebellion or injustice? Using historical examples from the Sahaba and Tabi'un, the author argues that such acceptance is permissible — but only if the judge is able to uphold justice. Without that condition, the appointment becomes forbidden because the very purpose of qada is defeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is accepting the office of qadi from an unjust ruler. Note that the ruling is not absolute but conditional on the ability to judge with truth.
The text initially presents the ruling as permissible, then immediately attaches the condition.
2
Examine the historical proof (dalil)
The author cites the practice of Sahaba (e.g., Abu al-Darda' accepting from Muawiya) and Tabi'un (e.g., Abu Burda accepting from Hajjaj). This establishes a precedent that acceptance is permissible despite the ruler's injustice.
The hadith about Ammar ibn Yasir confirms Muawiya's rebellion, yet Sahaba still accepted judgeships.
3
Identify the decisive condition
The text repeatedly stresses: acceptance is permissible only if the judge is able to rule with truth (qadā' bil-haqq). If not, it is forbidden.
This condition is the key differentiator. The purpose of qada is justice; if justice cannot be achieved, the act is futile.
4
Understand the rationale
The purpose (maqsad) of qada is to establish justice. If the judge cannot do so, the appointment fails its objective and becomes impermissible. Conversely, if he can, the benefit of justice outweighs the harm of association with an unjust ruler.
This reflects a broader Hanafi principle: means are judged by their ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الادب القاضي
اشرف البدایہ جلد نہم حضرت معاویہ کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء کا قبول کیا ہے اور حضرت علی کی باری میں حق خلافت حضرت علی کے ہاتھ میں تھا۔ اور تابعین نے حجاج کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کیا حالانکہ حجاج ظالم تھا۔ مگر یہ کہ قاضی قضاء بالحق پر قادر نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ مقصود ، عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنے سے حاصل نہ ہو گا۔ برخلاف اُس صورت کے جب قاضی اس پر قادر ہو۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح عادل اور برحق بادشاہ کی طرف سے عہد کا قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح ظالم اور غیر برحق بادشاہ کی طرف سے بھی عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ یعنی اگر کوئی شخص بغاوت کر کے غالب آ گیا اور فرمانروا ہو گیا۔ پھر کسی کو قاضی ہونے کیلئے مجبور کرنے لگا تو اس کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل میں فرمایا کہ شہادت عثمان کے بعد حق خلافت حضرت علی کے لئے تھا جیسا کہ اہل سنت والجماعت کا اس پر اتفاق ہے۔ لیکن حضرت معاویہ بن ابی سفیان نے حضرت علی کے خلاف بغاوت کی اور ملک شام کے حکمراں اور فرمانروا بن گئے ۔ علامہ ان الہمام نے حضرت معاویہ کی بغاوت پر استشہاد کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت عمار بن یاسر سے فرمایا تھا استفتلك الفئة الباغية تجھ کو عنقریب ایک باغی جماعت قتل کرے گی۔ حالانکہ عمار بن یاسر کو حضرت معاویہ کے ساتھیوں نے قتل کیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حضرت معاویہ اور ان کی جماعت کے لوگ بغاۃ میں سے ہیں۔ اور حضرت عائشہ ابتداء حضرت معاویہ کے ساتھ تھیں لیکن بعد میں حضرت عائشہ نے بھی ندامت کا اظہار کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن عبدالبر نے استیعاب میں تخریج کی ہے۔ قال قالت رضی الله عنها لابن عمر يا ابا عبد الرحمن ما منعك ان تنهانى عن مسيرى؟ قال رأيت رجلا غلب عليك يعني ابن الزبير فقالت اما والله لو نهيتني ما خرجت ) حضرت عائشہ نے ابن عمر سے فرمایا کہ اے ابو عبدالرحمن ! تجھ کو کس چیز نے روکا کہ تو مجھ کو میرے سفر سے روکتا ؟ ابن عمر نے کہا کہ میں نے دیکھا کہ تجھ پر ایک آدمی یعنی ابن زبیر غالب آ گیا۔ پس عائشہ نے کہا کہ بخدا اگر تو مجھے منع کرتا تو میں نہ نکلتی ۔ یہ اس وقت کا واقعہ ہے جب حضرت عائشہ حضرت معاویہ کی حمایت میں حضرت علیؓ کے خلاف جنگ کے ارادہ سے نکلی تھیں ۔ اور پھر جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث یاد آئی تو نادم ہو کر واپس تشریف لے آئیں۔ اس پر عائشہ نے ابن عمر سے کہا کہ اگر آپ ابتدا میں مجھ کو منع کر دیتے تو میں نہ نکلتی۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ”حق“ حضرت علی کی طرف تھا۔ بہر حال ان حکایات و روایات سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہادت عثمان کے بعد خلافت کا حق حضرت علی کو تھا مگر اس کے باوجود حضرت معاویہ کا حضرت علی کے ہاتھ پر بیعت نہ کرنا۔ اور ملک شام میں اپنی حکمرانی کا اعلان کرنا کھلی ہوئی بغاوت تھی۔ پس حضرت معاویہ کا سلطان جائر ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ اور تاریخ اس پر شاہد ہے کہ حضرت معاویہؓ نے صحابہ کو قاضی مقرر فرمایا ہے۔ اور صحابہ نے حضرت معاویہ کی طرف سے عہدوں کو قبول بھی فرمایا ہے۔ جیسے: حضرت ابوالدرداء کو شام میں قاضی مقرر فرمایا اور پھر ان کی وفات کے بعد انہی کے مشورہ کے مطابق فضالہ بن عبید انصاری کو والی شام مقرر فرمایا۔ اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ سلطان جائر کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دوسری دلیل میں فرمایا کہ حجاج بن یوسف مشہور ظالم فرمانروا گذرا ہے۔ مگر تابعین نے اس کی طرف سے بھی قضاء کے عہدے قبول کئے ہیں۔ مثلاً : حجاج بن یوسف نے ابو بردہ ابن ابی موسیٰ کو قاضی مقرر کیا۔ اور عبد اللہ بن ابی مریم نے اصفہان کا قاضی ہونا حجاج ہی کی طرف سے قبول کیا ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ظالم بادشاہ کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ظالم بادشاہ کی طرف سے عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنا جائز ہے لیکن اگر قاضی کے لئے حق کے ساتھ فیصلہ کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو قاضی ہونا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مقصود قضاء یعنی ملک میں عدل و انصاف جاری کرنا عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنے سے حاصل نہ ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر قاضی کے لئے حق کے ساتھ فیصلہ کرنا ممکن ہو تو عہدہ قضاء قبول کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
The Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Ashraf al-Bidaya Volume 9: He accepted the position of judge from Muawiya, and during Ali's turn the right of caliphate was in Ali's hand. And the Tabi'un accepted the position of judge from Hajjaj even though Hajjaj was oppressive. Except that the judge is not able to judge with truth. Because the purpose would not be achieved by accepting the position of judge. Contrary to the case when the judge is able to do so. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says: Just as it is permissible to accept the position of judge from a just and rightful king, similarly it is permissible to accept the position of judge from an oppressive and unjust king. That is, if a person rebels and overcomes and becomes ruler, then forces someone to become a judge, then accepting the position of judge from him is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah said in proof: After the martyrdom of Uthman, the right of caliphate was for Ali, as Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah agree. But Muawiya bin Abi Sufyan rebelled against Ali and became ruler of Syria. Allamah al-Hammam, citing Muawiya's rebellion, said that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) told Ammar bin Yasir: 'The rebellious group will kill you soon.' And indeed Ammar bin Yasir was killed by Muawiya's companions. So it is known that Muawiya and his group are among the rebels. And Aisha initially was with Muawiya but later expressed regret. As Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated in al-Isti'ab: She said to Ibn Umar: 'O Abu Abd al-Rahman, what prevented you from stopping me from my journey?' He said: 'I saw a man overcoming you, meaning Ibn al-Zubayr.' She said: 'By Allah, if you had stopped me, I would not have gone.' This is when Aisha set out to support Muawiya against Ali, then when she remembered the hadith, she returned regretful. So Aisha said to Ibn Umar: 'If you had stopped me at the beginning, I would not have gone.' This also shows that the truth was with Ali. In any case, from these stories and narrations it is known that after the martyrdom of Uthman, the right of caliphate belonged to Ali, but despite that, Muawiya not pledging allegiance to Ali and declaring his rule in Syria was open rebellion. So Muawiya is proven to be an unjust ruler. And history witnesses that Muawiya appointed Sahaba as judges. And Sahaba accepted positions from Muawiya. For example: He appointed Abu al-Darda' as judge in Syria, and after his death, on his advice, appointed Fadalah bin Ubayd al-Ansari as governor of Syria. This proves that accepting the position of judge from an unjust ruler is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah said in a second proof: Hajjaj bin Yusuf was a famously oppressive ruler. Yet the Tabi'un accepted positions of judgeship from him. For example: Hajjaj bin Yusuf appointed Abu Burda bin Abi Musa as judge, and Abdullah bin Abi Maryam accepted being judge of Isfahan from Hajjaj. This also shows that accepting the position of judge from an oppressive king is permissible. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Accepting the position of judge from an oppressive king is permissible, but if the judge is unable to decide with truth, then being a judge is not permissible either. Because the purpose of judiciary, i.e., establishing justice in the country, will not be achieved by accepting the position. Conversely, if the judge is able to decide with truth, then there is no harm in accepting the position of judge.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of accepting a judgeship from an unjust ruler. The author begins by stating that Sahaba accepted judgeship from Muawiya (whom he argues was an unjust ruler due to his rebellion against Ali) and Tabi'un from Hajjaj. However, a condition is immediately given: the judge must be able to judge with truth; otherwise, acceptance is impermissible because the purpose of qada — establishing justice — would be defeated. The commentary then provides an elaborate proof from history. First, it establishes that Muawiya was an unjust ruler by citing the hadith about Ammar ibn Yasir being killed by the rebellious group (bughat) and Aisha's regret after initially supporting Muawiya. Then it shows that despite this, Sahaba like Abu al-Darda' and Fadalah bin Ubayd accepted judgeships from Muawiya, proving permissibility. Second, it cites Hajjaj ibn Yusuf, a famously oppressive ruler, from whom Tabi'un accepted judgeships. The ruling is concluded by reiterating the condition: if the judge can rule with truth, it is permissible; otherwise, it is forbidden. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that necessity (here, the need for justice) can override the general rule of avoiding association with unjust rulers, but only if justice can actually be achieved.

Key Terms
سلطان جائر (sultan jā'ir): A ruler who is unjust or has attained power through rebellion rather than legitimate succession.
عہدہ قضاء (uhdah al-qadā'): The office or position of a judge (qadi).
بغاة (bughāt): Rebels against the legitimate ruler; in this context, Muawiya and his followers considered rebellious by the author.
قضاء بالحق (qadā' bil-haqq): Judging with truth and justice, according to Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for accepting a judgeship from an unjust ruler?
A) The ruler must be just.
B) The judge must be able to judge with truth.
C) The judge must be a Sahabi.
D) The ruler must be a caliph.

Key Takeaway
Accepting judgeship from an unjust ruler is permissible in the Hanafi school only if the judge is able to rule with truth; otherwise, it is forbidden.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Respecting Sahaba: The Ijtihadi Error and Prohibition of Unjust Labels
Intra-Hanafi critique of a ruling's expression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why it is impermissible in Hanafi fiqh to label a Sahabi as an unjust ruler when the disagreement is a matter of ijtihad, and identify the hadith evidence that supports the respectful treatment of Sahaba.

Core Idea
An ijtihadi error by a Sahabi is forgiven and rewarded; calling him unjust violates the respect owed to him.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi critique by Khadim, who objects to Sahib al-Hidayah's characterization of Muawiya as an 'unjust ruler'. Khadim argues that because Muawiya's opposition to Ali was based on ijtihad, and he was a Sahabi, such a label is inappropriate. This lesson examines the legal reasoning behind Khadim's objection, the hadith evidence, and the principles governing the treatment of Sahaba in Hanafi thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of critique
State what Sahib al-Hidayah wrote about Muawiya (i.e., presenting him as an example of an unjust ruler) and why Khadim objects.
2
Understand the concept of ijtihadi error
Define 'ijtihadi khata' – an error by a qualified mujtahid that is forgiven and even rewarded in Hanafi theology. Note that the caliphate of Ali was not a matter of nass but ijtihad.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Review the hadith from Tirmidhi (the Prophet's prayer for Muawiya to be a guide) and Bukhari (Ibn Abbas forbidding criticism). Understand how these hadith establish Muawiya's honor.
4
Apply the principle of Sahabi honor
Explain why Ibn Abbas, despite his own stature, considered it impermissible to criticize Muawiya solely because he was a Sahabi.
5
Consider the conclusion
Understand that Khadim attributes the inappropriate wording to a slip of the pen, preserving respect for Sahib al-Hidayah while correcting the expression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوائد خادم کے نزدیک حضرت معاویہ بن ابی سفیان رضی اللہ عنہ کو سلطان جائر کی نظیر میں پیش کرنا صاحب ہدایہ کے لئے کسی طرح مناسب نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ حضرت علی کا خلیفہ چہارم ہونا کوئی امر منصوص نہیں ہے، بلکہ مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ ہے۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ حضرت معاویہ کا حضرت علی کی مخالفت کرنا اجتہادی خطا تھی۔ اور مجتہد کی خطا معاف ہی نہیں بلکہ اس پر ایک اجر بھی ملتا ہے۔ پس جس خطا کو معاف کر دیا گیا ہو بلکہ اس پر اجر ملتا ہو اس کی وجہ سے جائر اور ظالم کے الفاظ استعمال کرنا صاحب ہدایہ جیسے عظیم المرتبت اور صاحب ورع حضرات کے لئے زیب نہیں دیتا۔ حضرت معاویہ نے اپنے اسلام کا اظہار اگرچہ فتح مکہ کے بعد کیا ہے لیکن عامتہ العلماء کا خیال ہے کہ حضرت معاویہ فتح مکہ سے بہت پہلے اسلام قبول کر چکے تھے ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ان کے والدین ابوسفیان اور ہندہ کی طرح ان کے واقعات میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور دیگر صحابہ کے ساتھ بغض و عناد اور اذیت رسانی کے واقعات نہیں ملتے ہیں ۔ امام ترمذی مناقب حضرت معاویہ بن ابی سفیان میں حضرت عبد الرحمن بن ابی عمیرہ کی روایت نقل کرتے ہیں۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے معاویہ کے بارے میں فرمایا: اے اللہ ! تو اسے ہدایت والا اور ہدایت پانے والا بنا اور اس کے ذریعہ لوگوں کو ہدایت دے۔ ابو ادریس خولائی کہتے ہیں کہ جب حضرت عمر بن خطاب نے مصر سے حضرت عمیر بن سعد کو معزول کر کے حضرت معاویہ کو اس کا والی مقرر کیا اور لوگ اس پر چہ میگوئیاں کرنے لگے تو حضرت عمیر نے فرمایا کہ معاویہ کا ذکر خیر سے کرو۔ کیونکہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے سُنا ہے کہ اے اللہ ! اس کے ذریعہ لوگوں کو ہدایت دے یا اس کو ہدایت دے۔ ان دونوں احادیث سے واضح ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی دعا کے احترام میں صحابہ نے بھی حضرت معاویہ کیلئے خفیف اور ہلکے الفاظ استعمال کرنے سے گریز کیا ہے بلکہ ذکر خیر کی تعلیم دی ہے۔ بخاری میں ہے کہ ابن ابی ملیکہ نے کہا کہ حضرت معاویہ نے عشاء کے بعد وتر کی ایک رکعت پڑھی۔ ان کے پاس ابن عباس کے مولیٰ ابن کریب بھی تھے۔ انہوں نے ابن عباس سے جا کر کہا۔ ابن عباس نے کہا کہ معاویہ پر نکیر کرنا ترک کر دو ۔ کیونکہ وہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابی ہیں۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا صحابی ہونا اتنی عظیم الشان دولت ہے کہ ابن عباس جو خاندان رسالت کے عظیم المرتبت صحابی اور رئیس المفسرین ہیں انہوں نے بھی حضرت معاویہ پر جرح کرنے کو روانہیں سمجھا۔ پس رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے معاویہ کو اللهم اجعله هادياً مهدياً واهد به کے ذریعہ دعا دینے اور حضرت عمیر کے لا تذکر معاویة إلا بخیر فرمانے ، اور حضرت ابن عباس کے دغه فانه قد صحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرمانے کے بعد ، صاحب ہدایہ کو حضرت معاویہ کے لئے جائر اور ظالم کا لفظ استعمال کرنے کی اجازت کیسے دی جاسکتی ہے۔
چونکہ صاحب ہدایہ بھی ہمارے بزرگ ہیں ، صاحب علم و فضل ہیں ، ورع اور تقویٰ کے مالک ہیں۔ اس لئے یہی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ سبقت قلم کا نتیجہ ہے۔ اور مصنفین اور مولفین سے اس طرح کی بھول ، چوک بعید از قیاس بھی نہیں ہے۔
In the opinion of Khadim, presenting Muawiya bin Abi Sufyan, may Allah be pleased with him, as an example of an unjust ruler is in no way appropriate for Sahib al-Hidayah. Because it is admitted that the fact that Ali was the fourth caliph is not a matter of explicit text, but rather a matter of ijtihad. At most it can be said that Muawiya's opposition to Ali was an ijtihadi error. And an error of a mujtahid is not only forgiven but earns a reward. So when that error is forgiven and even rewarded, using the words 'jair' (unjust) and 'zalim' (oppressor) does not befit great and pious people like Sahib al-Hidayah. Muawiya declared his Islam after the conquest of Mecca, but the general body of scholars holds that he had accepted Islam long before the conquest. That is why, unlike his parents Abu Sufyan and Hind, we do not find incidents of enmity and harm towards the Prophet and other Sahaba. Imam Tirmidhi, in the virtues of Muawiya bin Abi Sufyan, narrates from Abd al-Rahman bin Abi Umayrah that the Prophet said about Muawiya: O Allah, make him a guide and rightly guided, and guide others through him. Abu Idris al-Khawlani says: When Umar bin al-Khattab removed Umayr bin Sa'd from Egypt and appointed Muawiya as governor, people started talking. Umayr said: Speak only good of Muawiya, for I heard the Prophet say: O Allah, guide people through him or guide him. These two hadiths make it clear that out of respect for the Prophet's prayer, Sahaba refrained from using even light words about Muawiya and taught only good mention. In Bukhari: Ibn Abi Mulayka said that Muawiya prayed one rak'ah of witr after Isha. Ibn Abbas's freedman Ibn Kurayb was with him. He went to Ibn Abbas and told him. Ibn Abbas said: Stop criticizing Muawiya, for he was a companion of the Prophet. From this it is known that being a companion of the Prophet is such a great honor that Ibn Abbas, a great companion and chief of exegetes, considered it impermissible to criticize Muawiya. So after the Prophet's prayer for Muawiya, 'Allahumma ij'alhu hadiyan mahdiyyan wa ihdi bihi', and Umayr's statement 'La tadhkur Mu'awiya illa bi khayr', and Ibn Abbas's saying 'Dahhu fa innahu qad sahiba Rasul Allah', how can Sahib al-Hidayah be allowed to use the words 'jair' and 'zalim' for Muawiya? Since Sahib al-Hidayah is also one of our great scholars, knowledgeable, virtuous, and possessor of piety and taqwa, it can only be said that this is a result of a slip of the pen. And such mistakes from authors and compilers are not beyond possibility.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by Khadim (apparently a commentator) objecting to Sahib al-Hidayah's characterization of Muawiya as an 'unjust ruler' (sultan jair) in the previous lesson. Khadim argues that this is inappropriate because (1) Muawiya's opposition to Ali was a matter of ijtihad, and an ijtihadi error is forgiven and even rewarded, (2) Muawiya was a Sahabi and scholars like Ibn Abbas forbade criticism of him, and (3) the Prophet himself prayed for Muawiya to be a guide. Khadim provides hadith from Tirmidhi and Bukhari to support the respect due to Muawiya. He concludes that Sahib al-Hidayah's wording was a mere slip of the pen. This intra-Hanafi critique does not change the ruling itself but refines the language used in presenting the evidence.

Key Terms
مجتہد فیہ (mujtahid fīh): A matter that is open to ijtihad (independent reasoning) and not definitively settled by textual evidence.
اجتہادی خطا (ijtihadi khata): An error made by a qualified mujtahid in deriving a ruling; such an error is excusable and even rewarded in Hanafi theology.
صحابی (sahabi): A companion of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The text emphasizes their high status and that they should not be criticized improperly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Khadim consider it inappropriate to call Muawiya a 'sultan jair'?
A) Because Muawiya was not actually a ruler.
B) Because Muawiya's opposition to Ali was an ijtihadi error, and he was a Sahabi.
C) Because Muawiya repented later.
D) Because the Prophet forbade criticizing any ruler.

Key Takeaway
It is impermissible to label a Sahabi as unjust for an ijtihadi error; the Prophet's prayer and the respect of Sahaba establish this principle.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Protecting the Status of a Sahaba: Critique of Harsh Language in Hidayah
Defense of Muawiyah against accusation of being a wrongful judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why calling a Sahabi mujtahid 'ja'ir' or 'zalim' is impermissible in the Hanafi tradition, and cite the proofs establishing their lofty status.

Core Idea
A Sahabi's ijtihad error is forgiven; calling him 'wrongful' or 'tyrant' contradicts Ahl al-Sunnah respect.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah critiques a statement in al-Hidayah where Sadr al-Shariah described Muawiyah (RA) as a 'sultan ja'ir'. The commentator argues that such language is unbecoming because Muawiyah was a Companion and a mujtahid whose error is forgiven and even rewarded. The lesson explores the Hanafi position on respecting the Sahaba and the evidence supporting it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
What did Sadr al-Shariah state about Muawiyah in al-Hidayah? The commentator says he presented Muawiyah as an example of a 'sultan ja'ir' (wrongful ruler).
2
State the commentator's objection
Why is this problematic? The commentator argues that Muawiyah was a Sahabi and a mujtahid; his ijtihad error is forgiven and even rewarded, so calling him ja'ir or zalim is inappropriate.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
What proofs are cited? The Prophet's supplication for Muawiyah ('O Allah, make him a guide and guided, and guide others through him') and statements of other Sahaba (Umayr, Ibn Abbas) instructing to speak well of him.
4
Understand the Hanafi principle
Why is a mujtahid's error forgiven? In Hanafi usul, a mujtahid who errs receives one reward, and his error is not considered sinful. This principle protects the honour of Companions who engaged in ijtihad.
5
Conclude the correct position
The mufta bihi ruling is that using harsh terms like ja'ir or zalim for a Sahabi mujtahid is impermissible (makruh tahrimi). The passage suggests the Hidayah statement was a slip of the pen.

Book of Adab al-Qadi. 254. Ashraf al-Bidaya volume ... but being a qadi is not permissible because the purpose of qada, i.e., establishing justice and equity in the country, will not be achieved by accepting the office of qada. On the contrary, if it is possible for the qadi to decide with truth, then there is no harm in accepting the office of qada. According to Fawa'id Khadim, presenting Muawiyah ibn Abi Sufyan (may Allah be pleased with him) as an example of a wrongful ruler (sultan ja'ir) is not appropriate for the author of Hidayah in any way. This is because it is accepted that Ali being the fourth caliph is not a matter of text, but rather a matter of ijtihad. At most, it can be said that Muawiyah's opposition to Ali was an ijtihad error, and the error of a mujtahid is not only forgiven but he also receives a reward. So for an error that is forgiven and even rewarded, using the words 'ja'ir' and 'zalim' is not befitting for a great and pious person like the author of Hidayah. Although Muawiyah announced his Islam after the conquest of Mecca, the majority of scholars believe that he had accepted Islam long before the conquest of Mecca. Therefore, unlike his parents Abu Sufyan and Hind, there are no incidents of hatred, enmity, and persecution of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and other Companions in his accounts. Imam Tirmidhi narrates in the virtues of Muawiyah ibn Abi Sufyan from Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Umayrah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said about Muawiyah: 'O Allah, make him a guide and guided, and guide others through him.' Abu Idris al-Khawlani says that when Umar ibn al-Khattab dismissed Umayr ibn Sa'd from Hims and appointed Muawiyah as its governor, and people started gossiping, Umayr said: 'Speak well of Muawiyah, for I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: O Allah, guide people through him or guide him.' These two hadith make it clear that out of respect for the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), the Companions refrained from using light or disparaging words for Muawiyah and instead taught to speak well of him. In Bukhari, it is narrated that Ibn Abi Mulayka said that Muawiyah prayed one rak'ah of witr after Isha, and Ibn Abbas's freed slave Ibn Kurayb was with him. He went to Ibn Abbas and told him; Ibn Abbas said: 'Stop criticizing Muawiyah, for he is a Companion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' From this it is known that being a Companion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is such a great blessing that Ibn Abbas, who is a great Companion of the family of prophethood and the chief of exegetes, considered it inappropriate to criticize Muawiyah. So after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) supplicated for Muawiyah with 'Allahumma aj'alhu hādiyan mahdiyan wa ihdi bihi', and Umayr said 'lā tadhkurū Muʿāwiyata illā bi-khayr', and Ibn Abbas said 'daʿhu fa-innahu qad ṣaḥiba Rasūl Allāh ṣallā Allāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam', how can the author of Hidayah be allowed to use the words 'ja'ir' and 'zalim' for Muawiyah? Since the author of Hidayah is also a great scholar of ours, a person of knowledge and virtue, possessor of piety and God-consciousness, it can only be said that this is the result of a slip of the pen. And such mistakes and errors from authors and writers are not beyond possibility.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on a statement in al-Hidayah where the author (Sadr al-Shariah) refers to Muawiyah ibn Abi Sufyan (may Allah be pleased with him) as a 'sultan ja'ir' (wrongful ruler) and 'zalim' (tyrant). The commentator (Ashraf ul Hadaya) strongly objects, arguing that Muawiyah was a Companion of the Prophet and a mujtahid, and his opposition to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was an error in ijtihad, which is forgiven and even rewarded. Therefore, using such harsh terms is inappropriate. The commentator provides hadith proofs showing the Prophet's prayer for Muawiyah and the instruction of other Companions to speak well of him. The passage concludes that this was likely a slip of the pen from the author of Hidayah, who was otherwise a great and pious scholar.

Key Terms
جائز (ja'ir): A ruler or judge who acts wrongfully or unjustly
ظالم (zalim): One who commits injustice or oppression

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ashraf ul Hadaya, what is the ruling on calling Muawiyah (RA) a 'ja'ir' (wrongful ruler)?
A) Permissible because he opposed Ali (RA)
B) Impermissible because he was a Sahaba and mujtahid, and his error is forgiven
C) Permissible only if done by a scholar
D) Recommended as it shows adherence to truth

Key Takeaway
It is impermissible to call a Sahabi mujtahid 'ja'ir' or 'zalim', as their ijtihad errors are forgiven and they are honored by Allah and His Messenger.

Qada — Judiciary
beginner

Duty of New Qadi: Taking Possession of Court Records
Procedure for transfer of court records from previous to new qadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the transfer of court records (khara'it) from the previous qadi to the new qadi and explain the procedure for taking possession, including the handling of paper from different sources.

Core Idea
The new qadi must take possession of all court records, regardless of the source of paper.

When a new qadi assumes office, one of his first duties is to secure the records of the previous qadi. These records, stored in leather bags (khara'it), contain case files and other important documents. Without them, the continuity of justice could be broken. This lesson explains the ruling and procedure based on the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Duty
Recognize that the new qadi must ask about the diwan (the collection of khara'it) of the previous qadi. This is an obligatory initial action.
The diwan refers to the leather bags containing records, not a building.
2
Understand the Purpose
The records are kept as proofs (hujaj) for future cases. Therefore, they must be in the hands of the sitting qadi, not the dismissed one.
The records belong to the office, not the person.
3
Apply the Ruling on Paper Source
Regardless of whether the blank paper came from bayt al-mal, the litigants, or the dismissed qadi's own property, the correct view is that the new qadi takes possession.
In the latter two cases, the text asserts 'fi al-sahih' and 'huwa al-sahih'.
4
Outline the Procedure
The new qadi sends two trustees to take possession in the presence of the dismissed qadi. They review each document and categorize them into separate bags to avoid confusion.
The inquiry is for discovery, not to accuse the previous qadi.

Source Text

كتاب الادب القاضي
نئے قاضی کو اپنا عہدہ قضاء سنبھال لینے کے بعد کن امور کو انجام دینا ضروری
ہے۔ خرائط وسجلات کا معنی
قال ومن قُلّد القضاء يسال عن ديوان القاضى الذى كان قبله وهو الخرائط التي فيها السجلات وغيرها لانها وضعت فيها لتكون حجة عند الحاجة فتجعل فى يدمن له ولاية القضاء ثم ان كان البياض من بيت المال فظاهر وكذا اذا كان من مال الخصوم في الصحيح لانهم وضعوها فى يده لعمله وقد انتقل الى المولى وكذا اذا كان من مال القاضى هو الصحيح لأنه اتخذه تدينالا تمولا ويبعث امينين ليقبضاها بحضرة المعزول وامينه ويسأ لانه شيئا فشيئا ويجعلان كل نوع منها في خريطة كيلا يشتبه على المولّى وهذا السوال لكشف الحال لا للالزام
ترجمہ اور جس شخص کو قاضی مقرر کیا گیا وہ پہلے قاضی کا دفتر تلاش کرے۔ دیوان، چمڑے کے وہ تھیلے ہیں جن میں سرکاری فائلیں اور دوسرا ریکارڈ موجود ہو۔ کیونکہ ان فائلوں کو تھیلوں میں رکھا جاتا ہے تا کہ ضرورت کے وقت حجت ہوں۔ پس ان کو اس شخص کے قبضہ میں رکھا جائے گا۔ جس کو منصب قضاء حاصل ہو۔ پھر اگر سادہ کاغذ بیت المال سے ہوں تو ظاہر ہے۔ اور اسی طرح جب یہ سادہ کاغذ خصوم کے مال سے ہوں تو بھی صحیح قول کے مطابق یہی حکم ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خصوم نے ان کا غذات کو سابق قاضی کے ہاتھ میں اس کے عمل کرنے کے لئے رکھا تھا۔ اور حال یہ کہ عمل مولیٰ کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر معزول قاضی کے مال سے ہوں یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ قاضی معزول نے ان کا غذات کو بطور تدین کے مرتب کیا تھا۔ نہ کہ ذخیرہ اندوزی کے لئے۔ اور جدید قاضی دو امینوں کو بھیجے تا کہ وہ دونوں ان تھیلوں پر معزول قاضی یا اس کے امین کی موجودگی میں قبضہ کریں۔ اور وہ دونوں امین تمام کاغذات کو ایک ایک کر کے دریافت کر لیں ۔ اور دونوں امین ان میں سے ہر کاغذ کو علیحدہ تھیلے میں رکھتے رہیں تا کہ جدید قاضی پر اشتباہ نہ ہو۔ اور یہ سوال کشف حال کے لئے ہے نہ کہ
الزام کے لئے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جس شخص کو عہد ہ قضاء سپر د کیا گیا ہے اس کا سب سے پہلا کام یہ ہے کہ وہ معزول شدہ " قاضی سے ان تھیلوں کے بارے میں دریافت کرے جن میں سرکاری فائلیں اور ریکارڈ رکھا ہوا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ دیوان سے مراد چمڑے کے وہ تھیلے ہیں۔ جن میں بغرض حفاظت کوئی چیز رکھ کر ان کا منہ بند کر دیتے ہیں۔ پس قاضی کے پاس جو تھیلے ہوتے ہیں ان میں سجلات یعنی لوگوں کے مقدمات کی مسلیں رکھی جاتی ہیں۔ اور دوسری دستاویزات مثلاً اوقاف کی فائلیں رکھی جاتی ہیں ۔ اور شوہروں اور وارثوں پر جن لوگوں کے نفقات مقرر کئے جاتے ہیں ان کی تحریرات اور فائلیں بھی رکھی جاتی ہیں ۔ بہر حال خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ بحال قاضی معزول قاضی سے مذکورہ تھیلوں کے بارے میں اس لئے دریافت کرے گا کہ ان تھیلوں میں مقدمات کی مسلیں اور دوسری دستاویزات اس لئے دیکھی جاتی ہیں تا کہ بوقت ضرورت کام آئیں۔ لہذا ان کو موجودہ قاضی کے ہاتھ میں رکھا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اب تمام معاملات کا تعلق موجودہ قاضی سے ہے معزول قاضی سے کسی معاملہ کا کوئی تعلق نہیں رہا، وہ تو عام لوگوں کی طرح ایک فرد ہو گیا ہے۔
Ashraf al-Bidaya, Volume 9. 255. Book of Adab al-Qadi. What matters must a new qadi attend to after assuming the office of qada? Meaning of khara'it and sijillat. He said: The one who has been appointed qadi asks about the diwan of the qadi before him, which is the leather bags containing the sijillat (records) and other things. Because they are placed in them to be a proof when needed, so they are placed in the hand of the one who has authority over qada. Then if the blank paper is from the public treasury, it is apparent. Likewise, if it is from the property of the litigants, in the correct view it is the same ruling, because they placed them in his hand for his work, and now the work has transferred to the new master. Likewise, if it is from the property of the qadi himself, the correct view is the same, because he made them for piety, not for wealth. He sends two trustees to take possession of them in the presence of the dismissed qadi and his trustee, and they ask about them one by one, and they place each type in a bag so that they are not confused for the new master. This asking is for investigation, not for obligation. Translation: And the person who has been appointed qadi should search for the office of the previous qadi. Diwan are leather bags that contain official files and other records. Because these files are kept in bags so that they may be evidence when needed. So they will be placed in the possession of the one who holds the office of qada. Then if the blank paper is from the public treasury, it is apparent. And likewise, if the blank paper is from the property of the litigants, according to the correct statement the same ruling applies, because the litigants placed them in the hand of the previous qadi for his work, and now the work has transferred to the new master. And likewise, if it is from the property of the dismissed qadi, the correct view is the same, because the dismissed qadi prepared them as piety, not for accumulation. And the new qadi sends two trustees so that both take possession of these bags in the presence of the dismissed qadi or his trustee. And both trustees examine all papers one by one, and both trustees keep each paper in a separate bag so that there is no confusion for the new qadi. And this questioning is for discovery, not for obligation. Explanation: Imam Quduri says: The first task of the person who has been given the office of qada is to inquire from the dismissed qadi about these bags that contain official files and records. The author of Hidayah said that diwan refers to leather bags in which something is placed and the mouth is tied for protection. So the bags that are with the qadi contain sijillat, i.e., case files of people, and other documents, e.g., endowment files, and also documents regarding maintenance orders against husbands and heirs. In summary, the new qadi will inquire from the dismissed qadi about these bags because these case files and documents are kept for use when needed. Therefore, they will be placed in the hand of the current qadi, because all matters are now related to the current qadi, and the dismissed qadi has no relation to any matter; he has become like an ordinary person.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage provides the procedure for a new qadi upon taking office. Based on the matn of Quduri and the commentary of Hidayah and others, the new qadi must request the records (diwan/khara'it) from the previous qadi. These are leather bags containing case files (sijillat) and other documents. The ruling covers possession of paper: if it was from the public treasury (bayt al-mal), from the litigants, or from the dismissed qadi himself, in all cases the correct view is that the current qadi takes possession. This is because the files are for judicial work, which now belongs to the new qadi. The new qadi sends two trustees to take the bags in the presence of the previous qadi, review each document, and categorize them into separate bags to avoid confusion. This inquiry is for clarification, not to accuse the previous qadi.

Key Terms
خرائط (khara'it): Leather bags used to store official court records and documents
سجلات (sijillat): Court records, including judgments, case files, and other official documents
دیوان (diwan): The collection of leather bags (khara'it) containing the sijillat; also the office of records

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who takes possession of the court records (khara'it) after a new qadi is appointed?
A) The dismissed qadi retains them for his own records
B) The new qadi takes possession via two trustees
C) The litigants take back their documents
D) The public treasury (bayt al-mal) reclaims the paper

Key Takeaway
The new qadi must take physical possession of all court records (khara'it) regardless of the paper source, using two trustees to ensure proper handover.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
New Qadi Must Take Over Records from Predecessor
Ruling and commentary on transfer of court records

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on transfer of court records to a new qadi and explain why the Hanafi school requires handover even when the predecessor used his own funds.

Core Idea
Court records belong to the office of qada, not the person; they must transfer to the new qadi regardless of who paid for the paper.

The appointment of a new qadi raises a practical question: what happens to the case files and records accumulated by the predecessor? This passage from Al-Hidayah answers that question with a firm ruling that protects public interest. You will see how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to ensure continuity of justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the duty
What must the new qadi do according to the passage? He must inquire about the diwan (leather bags containing records) from the predecessor.
2
Examine the three scenarios
The paper for records could come from Bayt al-Mal, from the litigants, or from the qadi's own wealth. Determine the ruling for each.
3
Follow the correct ruling in each scenario
In all three scenarios, the correct view (sahih) is that the records must be handed over. Understand why even the qadi's personal funds do not give him ownership.
The key distinction is diyanatan (trust) vs tamwulan (ownership).
4
Note the minority opinion
Some Hanafi scholars hold that if the paper came from litigants or the qadi's own wealth, it is his property and he cannot be forced. Recognise why this is rejected.
The mufta bihi is the majority view from Al-Hidayah.
5
Understand the procedure
How should the transfer be executed? The new qadi sends two trustees to take possession in the presence of the removed qadi or his agent, examine files one by one, and categorise them into separate bags, then seal them.
This ensures clarity and prevents tampering.

قال ومن قُلّد القضاء يسال عن ديوان القاضى الذى كان قبله وهو الخرائط التي فيها السجلات وغيرها لانها وضعت فيها لتكون حجة عند الحاجة فتجعل فى يدمن له ولاية القضاء ثم ان كان البياض من بيت المال فظاهر وكذا اذا كان من مال الخصوم في الصحيح لانهم وضعوها فى يده لعمله وقد انتقل الى المولى وكذا اذا كان من مال القاضى هو الصحيح لأنه اتخذه تدينالا تمولا ويبعث امينين ليقبضاها بحضرة المعزول وامينه ويسأ لانه شيئا فشيئا ويجعلان كل نوع منها في خريطة كيلا يشتبه على المولّى وهذا السوال لكشف الحال لا للالزام
