ان کاغذات کے ذریعہ ذخیرہ اندوزی اور اپنے آپ کو مالدار بنانا مقصود نہیں تھا۔ پس جب یہ کا غذات اس کے پاس دیانت اور امانت کے طور پر تھے اور مال مملوکہ کے طور پر نہیں تھے تو جو بھی اس منصب پر آئے گا اُسی کو حوالہ کر دئیے جائیں گے۔ بعض حضرات کا خیال یہ ہے کہ اگر سارے کاغذات مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے مال سے خریدے گئے ہوں یا معزول قاضی کے مال سے خریدے گئے ہوں تو دونوں صورتوں میں معزول قاضی کو مذکورہ فائلیں اور دستاویزات دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اگر کاغذات قاضی معزول کے مال سے خریدے گئے تو معزول قاضی ان کا مالک ہے۔ اور اگر مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے مال سے خریدے گئے تو مدعی اور مدعی علیہ نے قاضی معزول کو ہبہ کر دئیے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں بھی معزول قاضی ان کا مالک ہے اور کسی انسان کو اس کی مملوکہ چیز دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اس لئے ان دونوں صورتوں میں قاضی معزول کو اس پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا کہ وہ مذکورہ کا غذات موجودہ قاضی کو سپر دکرے۔ لیکن صحیح قول وہی ہے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ ویبعث امینین الخ سے مذکورہ کا غذات سپرد کرنے کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد فرمایا کہ چارج لینے والا قاضی دو قابل اعتماد یا ایک قابل اعتماد آدمی کو معزول قاضی کی خدمت میں بھیجے تا کہ وہ معزول قاضی یا اس کے امین کی موجودگی میں تمام کاغذات اور فائلوں پر قبضہ کرے۔ اور موجودہ قاضی کا فرستادہ معزول قاضی یا اُس کے امین سے تمام فائلیں ایک ایک کر کے دریافت کر لے اور ہر قسم کے کا غذات کو علیحدہ علیحدہ تھیلے میں رکھتا رہے۔ مثلاً مقدمات کی مسلیں علیحدہ تھیلے میں رکھے اور اوقاف کی جائدادوں کی فائلیں علیحدہ کرے اور نفقات کی فائلیں علیحدہ رکھے۔ اسی طرح ہر قسم کی فائلیں الگ الگ کر کے رکھتا رہے۔ اور یہ ایسا اس لئے کرے گا کہ موجودہ قاضی پر کاغذات خلط ملط ہو کر مشتبہ نہ ہوں۔ موجودہ قاضی کے فرستادہ جب تمام کاغذات پر قبضہ کر لیں تو دونوں اس پر مہر لگا دیں تا کہ کمی، زیادتی
He said: One who is appointed as qadi should ask about the diwan of the qadi before him, which are the leather bags containing the records and other things, because they were placed there to be a proof when needed. So they are placed in the hand of whoever has the authority of qada. Then, if the blank paper was from the Bayt al-Mal, it is apparent. Likewise, if it was from the wealth of the litigants, in the correct view, because they placed them in his hand for his work, and it has transferred to the new master. Likewise, if it was from the qadi's own wealth, that is the correct view, because he took it as a religious duty, not for wealth. And he sends two trustees to take possession of them in the presence of the removed qadi and his trustee, and they ask about them one by one, and they place each type in a separate bag so that it is not confused for the new master. And this questioning is for discovering the situation, not for compulsion. Translation: And the person who is appointed as qadi should search for the office of the previous qadi. Diwan are leather bags containing official files and other records. Because these files are kept in bags so that they may be evidence when needed. So they will be kept in the possession of the person who has the office of qada. Then, if the blank paper is from the Bayt al-Mal, it is obvious. And similarly, when this blank paper is from the wealth of the litigants, according to the correct statement, the same ruling applies, because the litigants had placed these papers in the previous qadi's hand for his work, and the work has now transferred to the new master. And similarly, if they were from the removed qadi's own wealth, this is also correct, because the removed qadi had arranged these papers as a religious duty, not for hoarding. And the new qadi sends two trustees so that they both take possession of these bags in the presence of the removed qadi or his trustee. And those two trustees examine all the papers one by one, and they keep each paper in a separate bag so that there is no confusion for the new qadi. And this questioning is for discovering the situation, not for compulsion. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that the first thing for the person appointed to the office of qada is that he should ask the removed qadi about these bags containing official files and records. Sahib al-Hidayah said that diwan means leather bags in which something is placed for protection and their mouths are tied. So the bags in the qadi's possession contain sijillat, i.e., case files of people's lawsuits, and other documents such as waqf files, and records of maintenance fixed for husbands and heirs. In short, the new qadi will ask the removed qadi about these bags because the case files and other documents are kept in them to be useful when needed. Therefore, they will be placed in the hand of the current qadi, because all matters now relate to the current qadi, the removed qadi has no connection with any matter; he has become like an ordinary person. Then 'Thumma in kana al-bayad min bayt al-mal...' etc. is an answer to a question. The question is: These papers with writings on them should belong to the person who owns them, and all these case files should be given to him, not to the current qadi? The answer: These papers may have been given to the removed qadi from the Bayt al-Mal, or the plaintiff and defendant gave them, or they were bought from the removed qadi's own wealth. In the first case, it is obvious that the removed qadi should be compelled to hand over these papers, because whoever is appointed as qadi will be the possessor of official office items. So since the charge-taking qadi is the current qadi, these case files and all office records remain in his possession. And if all these papers were bought from the wealth of the plaintiff and defendant, then too the removed qadi will be compelled to hand over all papers to the current qadi, because the plaintiff and defendant had placed these papers in the removed qadi's possession because he was appointed to work on behalf of the caliph; but when the work and authority have transferred to the current qadi, these papers will also be handed over to him, and no paper will be left with the removed qadi. And if all these papers were bought from the removed qadi's own wealth, then too the removed qadi will be compelled to hand over all papers to the current qadi. This is the correct statement, because the removed qadi had kept these papers with himself as a trust and amanah, to protect people's affairs and their needs; he did not intend hoarding or enrichment through these papers. So since these papers were with him as a trust and amanah, not as owned property, they will be handed over to whoever comes to this office. Some people think that if all papers were bought from the wealth of the plaintiff and defendant or from the removed qadi's own wealth, then in both cases the removed qadi will not be compelled to give these files and documents, because if the papers were bought from the removed qadi's own wealth, then he owns them; and if from the plaintiff and defendant's wealth, then the plaintiff and defendant gave them as a gift to the removed qadi, so he owns them in that case too, and no one can be compelled to give away his owned property. Therefore, in these two cases, the removed qadi will not be compelled to hand over these papers to the current qadi. But the correct statement is the one mentioned by Sahib al-Hidayah. 'Wa yab'athu ameenayn...' etc. is an explanation of the method of handing over these papers. So he said that the charge-taking qadi should send two trustworthy men, or one trustworthy man, to the removed qadi, so that they take possession of all papers and files in the presence of the removed qadi or his trustee. And the current qadi's envoy should examine all files one by one from the removed qadi or his trustee, and keep each type of paper in a separate bag. For example, case files in one bag, waqf property files separately, maintenance files separately. Similarly, he should separate each type of file. He does this so that the papers are not mixed up and become confusing for the current qadi. When the current qadi's envoys take possession of all papers, both should put a seal on it to prevent any decrease or increase.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school, commenting on a statement by Al-Quduri regarding the duties of a newly appointed qadi. The author, likely from Ashraf al-Hidayah, expands upon the short matn with detailed explanation. The ruling: when a new qadi (al-qadi al-muwalla) assumes office, he must inquire about the diwan (leather bags containing records) from his predecessor (al-qadi al-ma'zul). The bags contain sijillat (court records), waqf documents, maintenance orders, etc., preserved as evidence. The new qadi must take physical custody of these bags. The text addresses three possible sources of the paper (blank or written): (1) from the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal) — obvious that it goes to the new qadi; (2) from the litigants' wealth — the correct view is also that it goes to the new qadi, because the litigants placed them in the qadi's hand for his official function, and that function has transferred; (3) from the removed qadi's own wealth — again the correct view is that he must hand them over, because he held them as a trust (diyanatan) for the benefit of people, not as his personal property (tamwulan). The passage then discusses a procedural question: why should the papers go to the new qadi even if the removed qadi owns them? The answer distinguishes between ownership and amanah — the papers were held in trust for the public interest. An alternative opinion (some scholars) holds that if papers were from litigants or from the qadi's own wealth, they are the qadi's property and he cannot be forced to give them. The correct opinion (as per al-Hidayah) rejects this and insists on transfer, relying on istihsan (juristic preference) because the public interest in preserving court records overrides private ownership, since the qadi held them for the function. Finally, the procedure: the new qadi sends two trustees (ameen) or one trustworthy person to the removed qadi's presence (or his deputy) to take possession, examine each item one by one, and categorize them into separate bags (e.g., case files, waqf files, maintenance files) to avoid confusion. The trustees should seal the bags to prevent tampering. This questioning is for clarity (kashf al-hal), not compulsion (ilzam). Thus, the legal weight: this is a mufta bihi ruling from al-Hidayah, with an alternative opinion mentioned but rejected.

Key Terms
دیوان (diwan): In this passage, leather bags used to store court records (sijillat) and other official documents.
خرائط (khara'it): Plural of kharita, meaning leather bags or sacks in which documents are kept for protection.
سجلات (sijillat): Plural of sijill, meaning official court records, case files, and judgments.
امین (ameen): A trustworthy person sent by the new qadi to take possession of the records from the removed qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the blank paper for court records was bought from the removed qadi's own wealth?
A) The removed qadi may keep them as his personal property.
B) The removed qadi must hand them over to the new qadi.
C) The new qadi must repay the cost to the removed qadi.
D) The records are destroyed to avoid confusion.

Key Takeaway
The new qadi must take custody of all court records from his predecessor, regardless of the source of the paper, because they are held in trust for the office, not as personal property.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Transfer of Court Records: Dismissed Qadi's Duty
Ruling on whether a dismissed qadi must hand over case files

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a dismissed qadi's obligation to transfer case files and distinguish the correct view from a dissenting opinion.

Core Idea
Court files are a trust, not property: the dismissed qadi must hand them over regardless of ownership.

What happens to court files when a qadi is replaced? Can the outgoing judge withhold files he bought with his own money? This passage from Al-Hidayah resolves the issue with a clear principle: judicial records are held as a trust (amanah) for the court, not as personal property. We will explore the three possible scenarios and why the correct view compels handover in all cases, along with the practical procedure for transfer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Recognize the question: who owns the case files? The owner might claim the right to keep them. The author explores three sources of paper: from the public treasury, from litigants, or bought by the qadi himself.
The dispute hinges on whether ownership overrides the duty to hand over.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each scenario
For all three scenarios, the Hanafi school (as per Hidayah) rules that the dismissed qadi must hand over all files. Understand the reasoning: in each case the files are a trust for the court.
This is independent of how the paper was acquired.
3
Analyze the dissenting view and its weakness
Some scholars argue that if papers were bought or gifted to the qadi, he owns them and cannot be compelled. Identify the flaw: the intention was not personal ownership but custodianship for the court.
The Hidayah rejects this ownership argument as inconsistent with the nature of the office.
4
Understand the practical procedure for transfer
The new qadi sends one or two trustworthy persons to receive the files, categorize them (cases, waqf, maintenance, etc.), and seal them to prevent tampering. The questioning is for information, not accusation.
This ensures integrity and continuity of judicial records.

کاغذات پر قبضہ کر لیں تو دونوں اس پر مہر لگا دیں تا کہ کمی، زیادتی کا امکان باقی نر ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ موجودہ قاضی کے فرستادہ حضرات کی طرف سے معزول قاضی سے سوال اور جرح کرنا محض معلومات حاصل کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ خدانخواستہ معزول قاضی پر الزام لگا نا مقصود نہیں ہے۔
Then, 'if the blank paper is from the public treasury etc.' is an answer to a question. The question is: these papers on which there are writings, whoever owns them should be the owner. And all these files and documents should be given to that owner, not to the current qadi? The answer is that these papers were either given to the dismissed qadi from the public treasury, or the plaintiff and defendant gave them, or they were bought from the dismissed qadi's own wealth. In the first scenario, the dismissed qadi is compelled to hand them over, because whoever is appointed as qadi will take possession of the office's official things. So since the taking-over qadi is the current qadi, the mentioned files and all office records will remain in his possession. And if all the mentioned papers were bought from the wealth of the plaintiff and defendant, even then the dismissed qadi will be compelled to hand over all papers to the current qadi, because the plaintiff and defendant gave these papers into the possession of the dismissed qadi on the condition that he is appointed to work on behalf of the caliph. But when authority and power are transferred to the current qadi, these papers will also be handed over to him. And no paper will be left with the dismissed qadi. And if all the mentioned papers were bought from the dismissed qadi's own wealth, even then the dismissed qadi will be compelled to hand over all papers to the current qadi. This is the correct statement. Because the dismissed qadi kept these papers with himself as a trust and an amanah, in order to protect people's affairs and their needs. Hoarding and enriching himself with these papers was not intended. So when these papers were with him as a trust and not as owned property, they will be handed over to whoever comes to this position. Some people's opinion is that if all papers were bought from the wealth of the plaintiff and defendant or from the dismissed qadi's wealth, then in both cases the dismissed qadi will not be compelled to give the mentioned files and documents. Because if the papers were bought from the dismissed qadi's wealth, then the dismissed qadi is their owner. And if they were bought from the wealth of the plaintiff and defendant, then the plaintiff and defendant gifted them to the dismissed qadi. In this case too, the dismissed qadi is their owner, and no one is compelled to give his owned property. Therefore, in both these cases, the dismissed qadi will not be compelled to hand over the mentioned papers to the current qadi. But the correct view is the one mentioned by the author of Al-Hidayah. 'And he sends two trustees etc.' is a description of the method of handing over the mentioned papers. Thus he instructed: the taking-over qadi should send two trustworthy or one trustworthy person to the service of the dismissed qadi, so that he takes possession of all papers and files in the presence of the dismissed qadi or his trustee. And the messenger of the current qadi should inquire about all files one by one from the dismissed qadi or his trustee, and keep each type of paper in a separate bag. For example, case files in one bag, waqf property files separately, maintenance files separately. Similarly, keep each type of file separate. He does this so that the papers are not mixed up and confused for the current qadi. When the messengers of the current qadi take possession of all papers, both should seal them to eliminate the possibility of increase or decrease. The author of Al-Hidayah says that questioning and cross-examination by the messengers of the current qadi towards the dismissed qadi is solely for obtaining information. God forbid, the intention is not to accuse the dismissed qadi.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the transfer of court records when a qadi is replaced. The author breaks down the issue based on who owned the paper files. In all three scenarios (papers from the public treasury, from litigants, or bought by the dismissed qadi), the correct view is that the dismissed qadi must hand over everything to the new qadi. The reason is that these papers are held as a trust (amanah) for the administration of justice, not as personal property. Even if purchased with his own money, the intention was to serve the court. The author contrasts this with some scholars who argue that ownership prevents compulsion, but he rejects that, affirming the Hidayah's position. The passage also details the procedure: the new qadi sends one or two trustworthy persons to receive the files, categorizes them, and seals them to prevent tampering. The questioning of the dismissed qadi is for information, not accusation. This ruling ensures continuity and integrity of judicial records, a key practical concern in Islamic judiciary.

Key Terms
معزول قاضی (ma'zul qadi): A judge who has been dismissed from his post.
امینین (aminayn): Two trustworthy persons sent by the new qadi to take possession of records.
دیانت و امانت (diyanat wa amanat): As a trust and depository, not as owned property.
بیت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury from which the dismissed qadi may have received paper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view as stated in Al-Hidayah, what must a dismissed qadi do with case files that were purchased with his own money?
A) He may keep them as his personal property.
B) He must hand them over to the new qadi because they are held as a trust.
C) He must destroy them to avoid confusion.
D) He may sell them to the new qadi.

Key Takeaway
Court records are a trust for the judiciary, not personal property; a dismissed qadi must hand them over to his successor regardless of how the paper was acquired.

Qada — Judiciary

New Qadi's Procedure with Prisoners from the Previous Judge
Ruling on investigating prisoners from previous qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure a new qadi must follow for prisoners from a previous qadi and distinguish when the previous qadi's statement is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
A dismissed qadi's word is not evidence; the new qadi must verify each prisoner's case independently.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical transition of authority in the judiciary. When a new qadi takes office, he inherits the prisoners of his predecessor. The ruling establishes that the dismissed qadi's statements are not automatically accepted; the new qadi must investigate each case. This ensures justice and prevents arbitrary detention based on unverified claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the new qadi's general duty
The new qadi is appointed as a supervisor (nazir) over Muslims' affairs. Therefore, he must investigate the situation of prisoners.
2
Classify prisoners based on their response
Prisoners fall into two categories: those who confess (iqrar) to a right owed, and those who deny the claim.
3
Determine the effect of confession
Confession (iqrar) is a binding proof. The new qadi enforces the confessed right and returns the prisoner to custody upon the claimant's request.
4
Determine the effect of denial
If the prisoner denies, the dismissed qadi's statement about the reason for imprisonment is not accepted without evidence (bayyinah). Dismissal reduces him to an ordinary citizen; his testimony alone is insufficient.
5
Handle absence of evidence
If no evidence is available, the new qadi should not release the prisoner hastily. He must make a public announcement (munadi) and investigate further, as the previous qadi's action is presumptively valid to protect the rights of others.
6
Note the inter-madhhab difference
Imam Ahmad holds that the dismissed qadi's word is still accepted because he is a trustee of Shari'ah. The Hanafi school rejects this, siding with Shafi'i and Malik.

He said: And he (the new qadi) looks into the situation of the prisoners because he is appointed as a supervisor. So whoever (among the prisoners) confesses to a right, he makes it binding upon him because confession is binding. And whoever denies, the word of the dismissed (qadi) is not accepted against him except with evidence, because by dismissal he has joined the subjects, and the testimony of a single individual is not a proof, especially if it is concerning his own action. Then if evidence is not established, he should not hasten to release him until he announces (a public call) about him and looks into his matter because the action of the dismissed qadi is apparently valid, so he should not hasten to release him so as not to lead to the invalidation of the right of another. Translation: And the new qadi should look into the situation of the prisoners because he is appointed as a supervisor. So whichever prisoner confessed to a right, he will make it binding on him, because confession is binding. And whoever denied, the statement of the dismissed qadi will not be accepted against him except with evidence, because the dismissed qadi, after dismissal, has joined the subjects. And the testimony of one individual is not a proof, especially if it is concerning his own action. Then if evidence is not established, the new qadi should not hasten to release that prisoner until he makes a public announcement about him and looks into his matter. Because the action of the dismissed qadi is apparently valid, so he should not hasten to release him so that it does not lead to the invalidation of the right of another. Explanation: Imam al-Quduri said that the new qadi, after taking charge, should first look into the situation of the prisoners. That is, he should send someone to the prison to find out their number and names, and ask them the reason they were put in prison. Because the qadi is appointed as a supervisor of the affairs and matters of Muslims, and the statement of the dismissed qadi is not proof. Therefore, investigating the conditions of the prisoners is necessary. And its method is that the new qadi should gather the prisoners and the plaintiffs. Then if a prisoner confesses to the right of his plaintiff against himself, the new qadi will make that right binding upon him. And if the plaintiff demands, he will be returned to prison. Because confession is a proof that makes the thing confessed binding upon the confessor. And when the plaintiff requests his imprisonment due to his right, he will be imprisoned. And if the prisoner denies the right of his plaintiff which is the cause of imprisonment, and the dismissed qadi reported the cause of imprisonment, then the statement of the dismissed qadi will not be accepted. Because the dismissed qadi, after dismissal, has become an individual of the subjects, and the testimony of one individual is not a proof, especially if it is concerning his own action, then a fortiori it cannot be a proof. Therefore, the statement of the dismissed qadi that I imprisoned him because he owes a just debt will not be a proof. This view is held by Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. And Imam Ahmad said that the statement of the dismissed qadi, even after dismissal, will be accepted just as it was accepted before dismissal, because he is a trustee of the Shari'ah. Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage addresses the new qadi's duty regarding prisoners inherited from his predecessor. The ruling is based on the principle that the dismissed qadi's word is no longer authoritative after his removal; he becomes like any other citizen. Hence, the new qadi must personally investigate each case. The key points: 1) If a prisoner confesses to the right of his claimant, the new qadi enforces that right and returns the prisoner to custody upon the claimant's request. 2) If the prisoner denies the claim, the dismissed qadi's statement about the reason for imprisonment is not accepted unless supported by evidence (bayyinah). This is because a single person's testimony is insufficient, especially about his own action. 3) If no evidence is available, the new qadi should not hastily release the prisoner; he must announce publicly about the case and deliberate, as the previous qadi's action is apparently valid. The passage also highlights a school difference: Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik agree with the Hanafi position that the dismissed qadi's word is not accepted. Imam Ahmad holds that his word is still accepted because he is a trustee of Shari'ah. The Hanafi position, however, is that dismissal severs that authority. This ruling ensures justice and prevents arbitrary imprisonment from being overturned without proper investigation.

Key Terms
محبوسین (mahbusin): Prisoners; individuals held in custody by the previous qadi.
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission by the prisoner of a right owed to the claimant.
بینہ (bayyinah): Clear evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
منادی (munadi): Public crier or announcement made about the prisoner's case to seek claimants or information.
حق غیر (haqq al-ghayr): The right of another person that may be affected by releasing the prisoner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a prisoner denies the claim against him and the dismissed qadi states the reason for imprisonment without evidence, what should the new qadi do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately release the prisoner based on the denial.
B) Accept the dismissed qadi's statement and keep the prisoner.
C) Not release the prisoner hastily; make a public announcement and investigate further.
D) Refer the case back to the dismissed qadi.

Key Takeaway
A new qadi must independently investigate each prisoner's case; the dismissed qadi's word alone is not proof, and release must not be hasty.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
New Judge's Duty: Investigation and Handling of Prisoners
Ruling with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios a new judge faces with prisoners and apply the Hanafi ruling that the removed judge's word is not accepted without evidence.

Core Idea
A new judge must investigate prisoners; the removed judge's word alone is not evidence.

When a new judge takes office, he inherits prisoners from the previous judge. He cannot simply accept the former judge's statements; instead, he must actively investigate each case. This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on how to handle prisoners who confess, who deny, and where no evidence exists, along with the reasoning based on the change in legal status of a removed judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Duty
The new judge is a supervisor (nazir) over Muslim affairs. He must first examine all prisoners and their causes of detention.
This duty is wajib (obligatory) upon assuming office.
2
Scenario 1: Prisoner Confesses
If a prisoner admits the right (e.g., debt) claimed against him, the judge enforces that right. Confession (iqrar) is a binding proof.
The prisoner may be returned to prison if the claimant requests.
3
Scenario 2: Prisoner Denies
If the prisoner denies the claim, the removed judge's word about the reason for imprisonment is not accepted unless supported by evidence (bayyinah).
After removal, the former judge is like any ordinary person; his single testimony is insufficient, especially regarding his own act.
4
Scenario 3: No Evidence
If no evidence is presented and the prisoner denies, the judge must not hastily release him. Instead, he must make a public announcement (nida') for several days to invite any claimant.
The rationale: the former judge's action is apparently correct, and quick release might harm an absent claimant's right.
5
Understand the Rationale and Dispute
The Hanafi position is that judicial authority terminates with removal. The removed judge's statement is analogous to a single person's testimony, which is not proof. Imam Ahmad holds that trusteeship continues, but the majority (Hanafi, Shafi'i, Maliki) disagree.
This difference leads to practical outcomes: Hanbali practice accepts the former judge's word; Hanafi requires evidence or announcement.

شہادت شاہدین سے حق ثابت کیا اور جدید قاضی ، شہود کی عدالت سے بھی واقف ہے تو قیامِ حجت کی وجہ سے قاضی جدید اس قیدی کو قید خانہ میں واپس کر دے گا ۔ اور اگر جدید قاضی ان کی عدالت سے واقف نہ ہو تو ان کے بارے میں معلومات حاصل کرے گا۔ پس معلومات کرنے پر اگر اُن کا عادل ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو بھی حجت قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اُس قیدی کو قید خانہ میں واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر قیدی کے خلاف بینہ پیش نہ کیا جاسکا یا مدعی حاضر نہیں ہوا۔ اور قیدی نے دعوی کیا کہ میرے خلاف کوئی مدعی نہیں ہے مجھے کو ناحق طور پر قید کر رکھا ہے۔ تو قاضی جدید اس کو رہا کرنے میں جلدی نہ کرے بلکہ چند روز منادی کرائے کہ قاضی کی طرف سے یہ اعلان کیا جاتا ہے کہ فلاں بن فلاں جو فلاں قید خانہ میں محبوس ہے اگر اس پر کسی کا کوئی مطالبہ ہو تو وہ حاضر ہو کر اپنا مطالبہ ثابت کرے۔ پس اگر مدعی حاضر ہو گیا [فیہا]۔ ورنہ قاضی چند روز تک یہ اعلان کراتا رہے۔ چند روز اعلان کرانے پر اگر مدعی حاضر نہ ہوا تو قاضی جدید محبوس سے کفیل بنفسہ لے کر اس کو رہا کر دے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیدی کے خلاف گواہ موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں قیدی کو جلدی رہا نہ کرنے کا حکم اس لئے دیا گیا ہے که قاضی معزول کا فعل یعنی اس کو قید کرنا بظاہر درست معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے جلدی رہا نہ کرے کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ مدعی غائب ہو۔ اور جلدی رہا کرنے سے مدعی کا حق باطل ہو جائے درانحالیکہ کسی کے حق کو باطل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
The new judge should examine the condition of prisoners because he has been appointed as a supervisor. Whoever confesses to a right, he imposes it upon him because confession is binding. Whoever denies, the word of the removed judge is not accepted against him except with evidence, because by removal he joins the rank of the subjects, and the testimony of a single person is not proof, especially when it concerns his own action. If no evidence is produced, he should not hasten to release him until he makes a proclamation and investigates his matter, because the action of the removed judge is apparently correct, so he should not hasten to avoid nullifying another's right. Translation: The new judge should look into the condition of prisoners because he has been appointed as a supervisor. So whichever prisoner confesses to a right, he will impose it upon him because confession is binding. And whoever denies, the removed judge's statement against him will not be accepted without evidence, because the removed judge by removal joins the subjects. And the testimony of one individual is not proof, especially when it is about his own action. Then if evidence is not established, the new judge should not hasten to release that prisoner until he makes a proclamation and looks into his matter. Because the removed judge's action is apparently correct, so do not hasten to release him lest it cause the nullification of another's right. Commentary by Sahib Quduri: The new judge, after taking charge, first examines the condition of prisoners, i.e., sends a man to the prison to find out their number and names, and asks them why they were imprisoned. Because the judge is appointed as a supervisor over the affairs of the Muslims, and the removed judge's word is not proof. So investigation of prisoners' situations is necessary. Its method is that the new judge gathers the prisoners and claimants. If a prisoner confesses to the right of his claimant upon himself, the new judge imposes that right upon him. And upon the claimant's request, he is returned to prison because confession is a proof that makes what he confessed to binding. And if the claimant requests his imprisonment due to his right, he will be imprisoned. And if the prisoner denies that right of his claimant which is the cause of imprisonment, and the removed judge informed of the cause, the removed judge's word will not be accepted because he has become a common subject and one person's testimony is not proof, especially when on his own action, so a fortiori it cannot be proof. So the removed judge's statement that he imprisoned him because a right was upon him is not proof. This is the view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik. Imam Ahmad said that the removed judge's word is accepted after removal just as before removal because he is a trustee of the Sharia. However, if the removed judge established the right through testimony of witnesses and the new judge is aware of their uprightness, then due to establishment of proof, the new judge will return the prisoner to prison. And if the new judge is not aware of their uprightness, he will investigate about them. Then if upon investigation they are found upright, even then due to establishment of proof, that prisoner will be returned to prison. And if no evidence is presented against the prisoner or the claimant is not present, and the prisoner claims there is no claimant against me and I am imprisoned unjustly, then the new judge should not hasten to release him but should announce for a few days: 'It is proclaimed on behalf of the judge that so-and-so son of so-and-so who is imprisoned in such prison, if anyone has a claim against him, let him come and prove his claim.' Then if a claimant comes, [then it is decided]. Otherwise, the judge continues the proclamation for a few days. After several days of announcement, if no claimant comes, the new judge takes a surety (kafil bi nafsih) from the prisoner and releases him. Sahib Hidayah says that the ruling not to release the prisoner quickly when there is no witness against him is because the removed judge's action of imprisoning him is apparently correct. So do not hasten to release because it is possible the claimant is absent, and quick release would nullify the claimant's right, and nullifying anyone's right is not permissible.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi discusses the duty of a new judge when he takes over judicial responsibilities. The passage begins by quoting the matn from Al-Hidayah stating that the new judge must examine the prisoners. The reason is that he is appointed as a supervisor (nazir) over the affairs of the Muslims. The ruling proceeds to detail three scenarios: (1) If a prisoner confesses to a right (e.g., a debt), the judge enforces it because confession (iqrar) is a binding proof. (2) If a prisoner denies the claim, the statement of the removed (former) judge about the reason for imprisonment is not accepted against the prisoner unless supported by evidence (bayyinah). The rationale is that upon removal, the former judge becomes like an ordinary subject; his word is akin to a single person's testimony, which is insufficient proof, especially when it concerns his own action (imprisoning someone). (3) If no evidence is available and the prisoner denies, the new judge should not hastily release him. Instead, he must make a public announcement (nida') for a few days to call any potential claimant. This caution is because the former judge's action of imprisonment is apparently correct (haqqan zahiran), and releasing him might invalidate a rightful claim. The passage then includes a detailed commentary by Sahib Quduri, who elaborates on the procedure: the new judge first sends someone to the prison to register the prisoners and their causes. He then gathers prisoners and claimants. If a prisoner confesses, the judge imposes the right; if the claimant requests imprisonment, the prisoner is sent back. If the prisoner denies and the former judge's statement is the only evidence, it is not accepted. This view is held by Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, while Imam Ahmad holds that the former judge's word is still accepted because he is a trustee (amin) of the Sharia. However, the Hanafi position (and that of the majority) is that it is not accepted due to the change in his status. The commentary further notes that if the former judge had established the right through witnesses and the new judge knows their integrity, the prisoner is returned. If not, the new judge investigates. If no evidence or claimant appears, the judge announces publicly and eventually releases the prisoner upon taking a surety. Finally, Sahib Hidayah reiterates the wisdom behind not releasing quickly: the former judge's action is apparently correct, and haste might injure an absent claimant's right. This entire discussion highlights the Hanafi principle that a judge's authority is personal and terminates upon removal; hence he cannot dictate judicial decisions thereafter.

Key Terms
محبوس (mahbus): A person imprisoned by the previous court
معزول (ma'zul): A judge who has been removed from office
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what must a new judge do if a prisoner denies the claim against him and no evidence is presented?
A) Release the prisoner immediately because his denial is sufficient.
B) Accept the removed judge's statement as proof and keep the prisoner imprisoned.
C) Announce publicly for several days to invite any claimant, then release upon surety if no one comes.
D) Refer the case back to the removed judge for further instructions.

Key Takeaway
A new judge must personally investigate prisoners; the removed judge's word is not proof, and release must not be hasty lest it invalidate an absent claimant's right.

New Judge and Deposits: Evidence Over the Removed Judge's Word
Juridical procedure for new judges handling deposits and endowment funds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a new judge's handling of deposits and endowment revenues, identify when the removed judge's word is accepted, and apply the rule to cases of conflicting acknowledgments.

Core Idea
A new judge relies on evidence or the possessor's acknowledgment, not the removed judge's word, unless the possessor confirms the judge's prior delivery.

When a new judge takes office, he inherits not only cases but also physical properties: deposits held by the court and revenues from endowments. How should he verify these assets? The passage from Al-Hidayah lays down a clear procedure: he must act based on evidence (bayyinah) or the acknowledgment of the person in possession. The removed judge's statement alone carries no weight, but an exception arises when the current possessor admits that the removed judge entrusted the property to him. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind these rules and their practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The new judge looks into deposits and endowment revenues. He acts according to evidence (bayyinah) or the acknowledgment (iqrar) of the person holding the property. This is the general rule.
Evidence here typically means testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females, as per Hanafi qada rules.
2
Understand why the removed judge's word is not accepted
The removed judge, once dismissed, becomes a commoner. His judicial authority is gone, so his mere claim about deposits is not proof. The school cites the general principle that a judge's word after removal is like any layperson's.
This is consistent with the earlier part (not in this excerpt) about prisoners.
3
Identify the exception and its rationale
If the possessor acknowledges that the removed judge handed the deposit to him, then the removed judge's statement about that deposit is accepted. Why? Because the possessor's acknowledgment retroactively proves that the deposit was lawfully in the judge's possession at the time of the alleged delivery. Thus, the removed judge's later acknowledgment (e.g., that he gave it to someone else) is valid as if the deposit were still in his hand.
The key is that the possessor's iqrar establishes the judge's prior yad (possession), making the judge's subsequent iqrar effective.
4
Analyze the sub-case of conflicting acknowledgments
If the possessor first acknowledges for someone else (claiming the deposit belongs to X) and later acknowledges the judge's delivery, the property goes to the first acknowledgee (X) because his right is prior. The possessor becomes a guarantor (damin) of its value for the removed judge, and that value is given to the second acknowledgee (the one from the judge's side).
This protects the prior established right and forces the possessor to bear the loss for his inconsistent statements.
5
Apply the rule to endowment revenues
Endowment revenues are treated similarly: the new judge acts on evidence or the acknowledgment of the person holding the funds. The removed judge's word alone is not sufficient, except under the same condition as deposits.
Endowment revenues must be spent according to the donor's conditions; the new judge ensures proper distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نیا قاضی امانتوں اور اوقاف کی آمد نیوں کیساتھ کیسا برتاؤ کرے
وينظر فى الودائع وارتفاع الوقوف فيعمل فيه على ما تقوم به البينة او يعترف به من هو في يده لان كل ذلك حجة ولا يقبل قول المعزول لما بيناه الا ان يعترف الذى هى فى يده ان المعزول سلمها اليه فيقبل قوله فيها لانه ثبت باقراره ان اليد كانت للقاضى فيصح اقرار القاضى كانه فى يده فى الحال الا اذا بدأ بالاقرار لغيره ثم اقر بتسليم القاضى فيسلم ما في يده الى المقوله الاول لسبق حقه و يضمن قيمته للقاضي ـاقراره الثان الى المقر له م من جهة القاضي
ترجمہ اور قاضی جدید ودیعتوں اور اوقاف کے حاصلات میں نظر کرے پس جس طور پر گواہ قائم ہوں اسی کے مطابق ان اموال میں عمل کرے یا جس شخص کے قبضہ میں ہو وہ اس کا اقرار کرے۔ اس لئے کہ ہر ایک حجت ہے۔ اور معزول قاضی کا قول قبول نہ ہو گا۔ اُسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے مگر یہ کہ جس کے قبضہ میں ودیعتیں ہیں وہ اقرار کرے کہ معزول قاضی نے اُس کو سپرد کی تھیں تو ان ودیعتوں کے بارے میں معزول قاضی کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ بعض کے اقرار سے ثابت ہوا کہ حقیقی قبضہ قاضی ہی کا تھا پس معزول قاضی کا اقرار صحیح ہوگا۔ گویا یہ ودیعتیں فی الحال اس کے قبضہ میں ہیں مگر جب کہ قابض نے پہلے دوسرے کے لئے اقرار کیا ہو۔ پھر قاضی معزول کے سپرد کرنے کا اقرار کیا ہوتو جو کچھ مقر کے پاس ہے وہ مقرلہ، اول کو سپر دکرے۔ کیونکہ اس کا حق سابق ہے اور اپنے اقرار ثانی کی وجہ سے قاضی معزول کے لئے اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اور یہ قیمت اس کو دیدی جائے گی جس کے لئے قاضی معزول کی جانب سے اقرار کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی جدید ، قیدیوں کی دیکھ بھال کے بعد اُن امانتوں کی دیکھ دیکھ کرے جو معزوال قاضی
How should the new judge deal with deposits and endowment revenues? And he examines the deposits and the revenues of the endowments, and he acts in them according to what is established by evidence, or what is acknowledged by the one who has them in his possession, because all that is proof. And the word of the removed judge is not accepted for the reason we mentioned, unless the one who has them in his possession acknowledges that the removed judge handed them over to him, then his statement regarding them is accepted, because it is established by his acknowledgment that the possession (yad) was the judge's, so the removed judge's acknowledgment is valid, as if they were in his possession at present. Except if he first acknowledged for another, then acknowledged the delivery of the judge, then he hands over what he has to the first acknowledgee due to the precedence of his right, and he guarantees its value to the judge – his second acknowledgment is for the acknowledged from the judge's side. Translation: The new judge looks into deposits and the yields of endowments. He acts in these funds according to what evidence establishes or what the person in possession acknowledges, because each is proof. And the removed judge's statement will not be accepted for the reason we have mentioned. Except that if the person who has the deposits acknowledges that the removed judge entrusted them to him, then regarding these deposits the removed judge's statement is accepted, because by his acknowledgment it is proven that the real possession was the judge's, so the removed judge's acknowledgment is valid, as if these deposits are currently in his possession. But if the possessor first acknowledged for another and then acknowledged the delivery of the judge, then whatever the acknowledgee has, he will hand it over to the first acknowledgee because his right is prior, and due to his second acknowledgment, he will be guarantor of its value for the removed judge. And this value will be given to the one for whom the acknowledgment was made from the removed judge's side. Commentary by Sahib Quduri: The new judge, after handling the prisoners, should look into the deposits that the removed judge [had]...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of the new judge's duties after taking office. The text from Al-Hidayah states that the new judge must also examine deposits (al-wada'i') and the revenues of endowments (irtafa' al-wuquf). He should act upon them according to evidence (bayyinah) or the acknowledgment (iqrar) of the person in whose possession they are found. The removed judge's word is not accepted because he has become a commoner, as explained earlier. However, there is an exception: if the current possessor acknowledges that the removed judge had previously handed the deposit to him, then the removed judge's word about that deposit is accepted. The reason is that this acknowledgment proves that the possession originally (or at that time) belonged to the judge, so the judge's later acknowledgment (e.g., that he entrusted it to someone else) is valid, as if the deposit were still in his hand. But if the possessor first acknowledged the deposit for someone else (e.g., claimed it belonged to a third party) and then acknowledged the removal judge's delivery, then the property goes to the first acknowledgee (the one with the earlier right), and the possessor becomes a guarantor (damin) of its value for the removed judge. This value is then given to the one for whom the acknowledgment was made on behalf of the removed judge. The commentary by Sahib Quduri begins to explain that after dealing with prisoners, the new judge should examine deposits held by the removed judge, but the passage is cut off. The underlying principle is that the new judge relies on objective evidence (either from witnesses or from the possessor's own admission) rather than on the removed judge's say-so, except when the possessor's admission retroactively validates the judge's authority over the property. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on verifiable proof and the protection of prior rights.

Key Terms
ودائع (wada'i'): Deposits or items held in trust by the previous judge or court
ارتفاع الوقوف (irtafa' al-wuquf): Revenues or proceeds generated from endowment properties
مقر (muqirr): The person who acknowledges or confesses (i.e., the possessor)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always accepted because he was the judge.
B) Never accepted after removal.
C) Accepted if the person holding the deposit acknowledges that the removed judge entrusted it to him.
D) Accepted only if two witnesses testify.

Key Takeaway
A new judge must rely on evidence or the possessor's acknowledgment regarding deposits and endowment revenues; the removed judge's word alone is insufficient, except when the possessor confirms the judge's prior delivery.

New Judge's Handling of a Previously Imprisoned Person
Ruling on procedure for new judge regarding prisoner from previous judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure a new Hanafi judge must follow when dealing with a prisoner from a previous judge and apply it to a scenario involving verification of witnesses and absent claimants.

Core Idea
A new judge must not hastily release a prisoner; he must verify evidence and announce for absent claimants.

When a new judge takes over, he inherits cases from the previous judge. This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi outlines the careful procedure he must follow for a prisoner who was already jailed. The ruling balances the apparent correctness of the previous judge's action with the protection of absent claimants' rights. We will walk through the analytical steps to understand the conditions and actions required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The new judge finds a prisoner from the previous judge. Determine whether there are witnesses who testified against the prisoner and whether the claimant is present.
2
Check the witnesses' integrity
If the new judge knows the witnesses to be upright (adil), or investigates and finds them so, the proof stands and the prisoner remains jailed.
3
Handle absence of evidence or claimant
If no witnesses exist or the claimant does not appear, the prisoner may claim false imprisonment.
4
Implement the announcement procedure
The judge must make a public announcement for several days calling for any claimant to come forward.
5
Release with guarantor
After several days of announcements with no claimant, the judge takes a personal guarantor (kafil bi-nafsihi) and releases the prisoner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شہادت شاہدین سے حق ثابت کیا اور جدید قاضی ، شہود کی عدالت سے بھی واقف ہے تو قیامِ حجت کی وجہ سے قاضی جدید اس قیدی کو قید خانہ میں واپس کر دے گا ۔ اور اگر جدید قاضی ان کی عدالت سے واقف نہ ہو تو ان کے بارے میں معلومات حاصل کرے گا۔ پس معلومات کرنے پر اگر اُن کا عادل ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو بھی حجت قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اُس قیدی کو قید خانہ میں واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر قیدی کے خلاف ہینہ پیش نہ کیا جاسکا یا مدعی حاضر نہیں ہوا۔ اور قیدی نے دعوی کیا کہ میرے خلاف کوئی مدعی نہیں ہے مجھے کو ناحق طور پر قید کر رکھا ہے۔ تو قاضی جدید اس کو رہا کرنے میں جلدی نہ کرے بلکہ چند روز منادی کرائے کہ قاضی کی طرف سے یہ اعلان کیا جاتا ہے کہ فلاں بن فلاں جو فلاں قید خانہ میں محبوس ہے اگر اس پر کسی کا کوئی مطالبہ ہو تو وہ حاضر ہو کر اپنا مطالبہ ثابت کرے۔ پس اگر مدعی حاضر ہو گیا فیہا ۔ ورنہ قاضی چند روز تک یہ اعلان کراتا رہے۔ چند روز اعلان کرانے پر اگر مدعی حاضر نہ ہوا تو قاضی جدید محبوس سے کفیل بنفسہ لے کر اس کو رہا کر دے۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیدی کے خلاف گواہ موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں قیدی کو جلدی رہا نہ کرنے کا حکم اس لئے دیا گیا ہے که قاضی معزول کا فعل یعنی اس کو قید کرنا بظاہر درست معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے جلدی رہا نہ کرے کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ مدعی غائب ہو۔ اور جلدی رہا کرنے سے مدعی کا حق باطل ہو جائے درانحالیکہ کسی کے حق کو باطل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
The right was established through the testimony of witnesses, and the new judge is also aware of the witnesses' integrity, so due to the establishment of proof, the new judge will return this prisoner to prison. And if the new judge is not aware of their integrity, he will investigate them. Then after investigation, if their uprightness is proven, even then, due to the establishment of proof, that prisoner will be returned to prison. And if no evidence can be presented against the prisoner, or the claimant does not appear, and the prisoner claims that there is no claimant against him and that he is being imprisoned unjustly, then the new judge should not hasten to release him. Instead, he should make an announcement for several days: 'On behalf of the judge, it is announced that so-and-so son of so-and-so, who is imprisoned in such-and-such prison, if anyone has a claim against him, let them come and prove their claim.' So if the claimant appears, then [fine]. Otherwise, the judge continues this announcement for several days. After announcing for several days, if no claimant appears, then the new judge takes a guarantor for the person (kafil bi-nafsihi) and releases him.

The author of al-Hidayah says: The ruling not to release the prisoner quickly in the absence of witnesses against him is given because the action of the removed judge (i.e., imprisoning him) apparently seems correct. Therefore, do not release him quickly because it is very possible that the claimant is absent. And releasing him quickly would nullify the claimant's right, whereas nullifying someone's right is not permissible.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on the etiquette of the judge (Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi) addresses the procedure a new judge must follow when dealing with a prisoner who was imprisoned by the previous, now-removed judge. The passage is a ruling with rational proof (dalil aqli based on maslaha). The new judge first checks the status of the witnesses who testified against the prisoner. If the witnesses were found to be upright (adil), the proof stands, and the prisoner remains jailed. If the new judge does not know the witnesses, he must investigate their integrity. If they are proven upright, again the proof stands. However, if no witnesses or claimant appear, the prisoner may claim false imprisonment. In that case, the judge must not immediately release him; rather, he must make a public announcement for several days to allow any potential claimant to come forward. Only after no claimant appears after several days of announcements may the judge release the prisoner, and even then, he must take a personal guarantor (kafil bi-nafsihi) to ensure the prisoner's availability if a claim later arises. The reason given by the author of al-Hidayah is that the former judge's action (imprisonment) is apparently correct, so hasty release could prejudice an absent claimant's right, which is impermissible.

Key Terms
قاضی جدید (qāḍī jadīd): The newly appointed judge who takes over from the removed judge.
کفیل بنفسہ (kafīl bi-nafsihi): A guarantor who guarantees the presence of the released prisoner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the new judge do if no witnesses or claimant are present for a prisoner?
A) Immediately release the prisoner
B) Keep the prisoner indefinitely
C) Make a public announcement for several days before taking a guarantor and releasing
D) Send the prisoner to another city

Key Takeaway
A new Hanafi judge must not hastily release a prisoner; he must verify evidence and announce for absent claimants to protect their rights.

New Judge's Dealing with Deposits and Endowment Proceeds
Ruling on how new judge acts on evidence and admissions regarding deposits and endowments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for when the new judge accepts or rejects the removed judge's statement regarding deposits and endowments, and apply it to scenarios involving evidence (bayyinah) and admission (iqrar).

Core Idea
The new judge acts on evidence or the custodian's admission; the removed judge's word alone is not proof.

When a new judge takes office, he must oversee deposits and endowment proceeds. The key question is: what proofs can he rely on? This lesson clarifies that he must base his decisions on valid legal evidence or the admission of the person currently holding the property. The removed judge's statement is generally not accepted, unless the custodian confirms that the removed judge entrusted the property to him. This ensures that decisions are grounded in reliable proofs and prevents arbitrary changes in ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary proofs
Recognize that the new judge acts upon bayyinah (witness testimony) or the iqrar (admission) of the custodian. Both are considered valid legal proofs (hujjah).
2
State the default rule for the removed judge
The statement of the removed judge (al-ma'zul) is not accepted because he is no longer in authority and his word alone is not a proof.
This is based on the principle that a single individual's statement is not a hujjah.
3
Identify the exception
If the custodian admits that the removed judge entrusted the property to him, then the removed judge's statement becomes acceptable. The admission proves the original control (yad) was with the removed judge.
This exception applies only when the custodian's admission corroborates the removed judge's claim.
4
Analyze conflicting admissions
If the custodian first admits for one person (e.g., Khalid) and later admits delivery by the removed judge, he must honor the earlier admission due to precedence. He then becomes liable to the removed judge for the property's value.
This protects the right of the first claimant.
5
Apply to a simple example
Consider: New judge finds a deposit with Khalid. Witnesses say it belongs to Hamid. The judge orders Khalid to give it to Hamid. If Khalid admits it belongs to Hamid, same result. If removed judge claims it belongs to someone else without Khalid's admission, the judge rejects that claim.

He (the new judge) examines the deposits and the proceeds of endowments, and acts upon that which is established by evidence (bayyinah) or that which is admitted by the person in whose possession it is, because all of that is a proof (hujjah). And the statement of the removed judge (al-ma'zul) is not accepted, for the reason we have explained, unless the person in whose possession it is admits that the removed judge entrusted it to him. Then his statement is accepted concerning them, because by his admission it is established that the control (yad) was with the judge, so the judge's admission becomes valid, as if it were in his hand at present. Except if he (the custodian) first made an admission for someone else, then later admitted the delivery by the removed judge, then he delivers what is in his hand to the first person to whom he admitted, due to the precedence of his right, and he becomes liable for its value for the removed judge in his second admission to the person to whom he admitted on behalf of the removed judge.

Translation: And the new judge examines the deposits and the proceeds of endowments. Then he acts upon these properties in accordance with the witnesses that are established, or the admission of the person in whose possession it is. Because each of these is a proof. And the statement of the removed judge will not be accepted, for the same reason we have already explained. Except that the person in whose possession the deposits are admits that the removed judge entrusted them to him, then the removed judge's statement concerning these deposits will be accepted. Because by his admission it is proven that the real control was with the judge, so the removed judge's admission will be valid, as if these deposits are currently in his possession. But if the possessor first made an admission for someone else, then later admitted the delivery by the removed judge, then what the possessor has will be handed over to the first person to whom he admitted, because his right has precedence. And due to his second admission, he will be liable for its value (or its equivalent) for the removed judge. Then that equivalent or value will be given to the person for whom the removed judge made the admission.

Elaboration: Imam al-Quduri says: The new judge, after attending to the prisoners, should examine the trusts (amanat) that the removed judge had placed with his trustees. He should also examine the income and expenditure of endowments, to see if the endowment income is distributed according to the conditions and whether the trustees are misappropriating endowment properties. So the new judge acts in the properties of trusts and endowments in accordance with the testimony of witnesses. For example, if testimony is given that the trust in Khalid's possession belongs to Hamid, the new judge will make Khalid give that trust to Hamid. Or if the possessor admits, 'This trust in my possession belongs to so-and-so,' the new judge will act according to that admission. The reason for acting according to testimony or the possessor's admission is that for the new judge to act, the existence of a valid legal proof (hujjah shar'iyyah) is necessary. And testimony and the possessor's admission are both valid legal proofs. Therefore, the new judge will act according to testimony and is bound to act according to the possessor's admission. And if the removed judge says something contrary to the possessor, for example, the removed judge says that Khalid has a trust of one thousand rupees belonging to Hamid, and Khalid denies it and says the thousand rupees are his, then in this case the removed judge's statement is not accepted, because upon being removed he becomes a common individual under the rule, and the statement of a lone individual is not a proof. So his statement is not accepted. Yes, if the possessor admits, 'This trust was entrusted to me by the removed judge and I do not know to whom it belongs,' or the possessor says, 'This trust was entrusted to me by the removed judge and it belongs to so-and-so,' and the removed judge also admits for him, then in both these cases the removed judge's statement is accepted, because by the possessor's admission it is proven that the original control of the trust was with the removed judge. And when the original control was with the removed judge, it is as if the mentioned trust is currently in the removed judge's possession. And since in matters of trust, the statement of the trustee (i.e., the possessor) is reliable, therefore in both mentioned cases the removed judge's statement is accepted. And if the possessor (i.e., the trustee) first admitted, 'This property in my possession is a trust from Khalid,' then later admitted, 'This property was entrusted to me by the removed judge,' and the removed judge admits for someone other than Khalid, then the possessor will be ordered to hand over this property to Khalid, the one for whom he first admitted, because his right is prior due to the earlier admission. And second, due to his admission of delivery by the removed judge, he will be liable to the removed judge for its equivalent (if it is a fungible) or its value (if it is a non-fungible). Then the removed judge will give that equivalent or value to the person for whom the removed judge made the admission.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage expands upon the duties of the new judge regarding deposits (wada'i') and endowment proceeds (irtafa' al-wuquf). The ruling: the new judge must act based on either evidence (bayyinah) or the admission of the person currently in possession of the property. The statement of the removed judge (al-ma'zul) is not accepted because he is no longer a judge and his word alone is not a hujjah. However, an exception is made: if the possessor admits that the removed judge had entrusted the property to him, then the removed judge's statement about the ownership is accepted, because the admission proves the original control was with the removed judge, making his admission as if the property were currently in his hand. A further scenario: if the possessor first admits for one person (e.g., Khalid) and then later admits delivery by the removed judge, he must first honor the earlier admission, and he becomes liable to the removed judge for the property's value. This ensures that rights are prioritized and that the removed judge's admission is binding only when consistent with the possessor's admission. Imam al-Quduri is cited to emphasize that the new judge must diligently oversee all trusts and endowments, ensuring no misappropriation.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadī'ah): Deposits or trusts held by trustees
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, specifically witness testimony
اقرار (iqrār): Admission or confession of a party

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The new judge must base decisions on evidence or the custodian's admission; the removed judge's word alone carries no weight unless the custodian corroborates it.

The Permissibility of a Judge Sitting in the Mosque for Judgment: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi vs. Shafi'i dispute on judge sitting in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on judges sitting in mosques, explain the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi rebuttal using dalil and qiyas.

Core Idea
Judges may sit in mosques for judgment because it is an act of worship, like prayer.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the permissibility of a judge holding court inside a mosque. The Hanafi school holds it is recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah), while al-Shafi'i considers it disliked (makruh). The Hanafi response relies on textual proof from the Prophet's practice and qiyas, addressing the Shafi'i concerns about ritual purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The text opens with the Hanafi position: the judge should sit visibly in the mosque, preferably the congregational mosque. Identify the precise hukm level (sunnah mu'akkadah) and the reasoning: so the judge is easily found.
The phrase 'He said' refers to al-Quduri's matn.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues it is makruh because polytheists (mushrik) might enter (impure by text) and menstruating women (who are prohibited from entering). This is a purity-based objection.
The Shafi'i view is based on avoiding ritual impurity in the mosque.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttals
The Hanafi response has three parts: (1) a hadith 'Mosques were built for dhikr and judgment', (2) the Prophet settled disputes in his mu'takaf and the caliphs did likewise, (3) judgment is an act of worship like prayer. Then the refutation of the impurity objections: polytheist impurity is spiritual, not physical; menstruating women inform the judge who can go out.
The rebuttal uses both naqli (hadith, practice) and aqli (qiyas) arguments.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The dispute leads to a difference in practice: Hanafi judges may hold court in the mosque; Shafi'i judges should avoid it. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
The tarjih (preferred view) in the Hanafi school is the permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجلس للحكم جلوساً ظاهراً في المسجد كيلا يشتبه مكانه على الغرباء بعض المقيمين والمسجد الجامع اولى لانه اشهر و قال الشافعى يكره الجلوس فى المسجد للقضاء لانه يحضره المشرك وهو نجس بالنص والحائض وهى ممنوعة عن دخوله ولنا قوله عليه السلام انما بنيت المساجد لذكر الله تعالى والحكم وكان رسول الله يفصل الخصومة فى معتكفه وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون كانوا يجلسون في المساجد لفصل الخصومات ولان القضاء عبادة فيجوز اقامتها في المسجد كالصلوة و نجاسة المشرك في اعتقاده لا في ظاهره فلا يمنع من دخوله والحائض تخبر بحالها فيخرج القاضى اليها او الى باب
He said: He sits for judgment with a visible sitting in the mosque, so that his location is not confused for visitors and some residents. The congregational mosque (al-masjid al-jami') is more preferable because it is more famous. And al-Shafi'i said: It is disliked (makruh) to sit in the mosque for judgment because the polytheist (mushrik) attends it, and he is impure (najis) by text, and the menstruating woman (ha'id) who is prohibited from entering it. And our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'The mosques were only built for the remembrance of Allah, the Exalted, and for judgment.' And the Messenger of Allah used to settle disputes in his place of seclusion (mu'takaf), and likewise the Rightly Guided Caliphs used to sit in mosques for settling disputes. And because judgment is an act of worship, so it is permissible to perform it in the mosque like prayer. And the impurity of the polytheist is in his belief, not in his apparent state, so it does not prevent his entry. And the menstruating woman informs of her condition, so the judge goes out to her or to the door.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage records a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the permissibility of a judge holding court inside a mosque. The Hanafi position (from the text: 'He said' refers to al-Quduri) is that the judge should sit visibly in the mosque, preferably the main congregational mosque (masjid jami'), so that litigants and the public can easily find him. The Shafi'i position is that it is makruh because the mosque may be entered by polytheists, who are ritually impure according to the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-Mushrikun?), and by menstruating women, who are prohibited from entering. The Hanafi response is threefold: (1) There is a hadith that mosques are built for dhikr and judgment. (2) The Prophet himself settled disputes in his place of seclusion (mu'takaf) and the caliphs did the same. (3) Judgment is an act of worship like prayer, so it is permissible in the mosque. As for the polytheist's impurity, it is spiritual, not physical, so it doesn't prevent entry; the judge can deal with menstruating women by going out to them when necessary. This is a classic example of inter-madhhab dispute where both sides use textual evidence and qiyas.

Key Terms
مسجد جامع (masjid jāmi'): The main congregational mosque where Friday prayers are held
مشرك (mushrik): Polytheist, one who associates partners with Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the Hanafi proof for a judge sitting in the mosque?
A) It is easier for the judge
B) The mosque is the most honored place
C) The Prophet settled disputes in his place of seclusion
D) The mosque is always empty

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits judges to sit in mosques for judgment, based on prophetic practice and analogy to prayer, rebutting the Shafi'i purity concerns.

New Qadi's Duty to Act on Testimony and Acknowledgment in Trust Cases
Ruling on new qadi's action based on testimony or acknowledgment regarding trusts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a new judge must act on testimony or the custodian's acknowledgment in trust disputes, and apply the exceptions regarding the removed judge's statement.

Core Idea
Testimony and the custodian's acknowledgment are binding proofs; a removed judge's word alone is not.

When a new qadi takes office, he inherits unresolved trust and endowment cases. This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya clarifies his obligations: he must supervise endowment finances and resolve trust disputes based on clear legal proof. The primary proofs are testimony (shahada) and the custodian's own acknowledgment (iqrar). However, the statements of the removed judge are generally not accepted unless the custodian acknowledges his involvement. This lesson breaks down the rule, the exceptions, and the priority rule when acknowledgments conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the new judge's general duty
The passage begins by stating that the new judge must supervise the income and expenditure of awqaf and ensure trustees do not usurp properties. Then, it focuses on trusts: he must act based on legal proof.
This establishes the judge's supervisory and adjudicative role.
2
Recognize the two valid proofs
The text explicitly states that testimony (bayyinah) and the custodian's acknowledgment (iqrar) are each a legal proof (hujja shar'iyya). The new judge is bound to act upon them.
Both are equally binding; no preference is given between them in the basic rule.
3
Apply the rule to a simple case
The example: if witnesses testify that a trust with Khalid belongs to Hamid, the judge must deliver it to Hamid. Similarly, if the custodian acknowledges the trust belongs to a specific person, the judge acts accordingly.
This illustrates straightforward application.
4
Analyze the removed judge's statements
After removal, the judge becomes an ordinary subject. His claim against a custodian is not accepted because a single person's word is not proof. However, if the custodian acknowledges the removed judge's involvement (e.g., entrusted the property), then the removed judge's statement is accepted along with the custodian's.
The exception requires the custodian's acknowledgment to give weight to the removed judge's statement.
5
Determine priority when acknowledgments conflict
If the custodian first acknowledges for one person (e.g., Khalid) and later acknowledges the property was from the removed judge who claims for another, the earlier acknowledgment takes precedence. The property goes to Khalid, and the custodian becomes guarantor to the removed judge, who then compensates his claimant.
This resolves conflicts and ensures priority of earlier rights.
